                <li class="_3v_7" role="menuitem" data-reactid="405"><a class="" href="https://auth0.com/blog/tech/" rel="external" data-reactid="406"><span class="-gCQ" data-reactid="407">
                   <!-- react-text: 408 -->Auth0 Blog

         <div data-reactid="488">
          <div class="api-section" data-section="none"> 
           <h1 id="introduction" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Introduction</h1> 
           <p>The Authentication API exposes the identity functionality of Auth0, as well as the supported identity protocols like <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/protocols/oidc">OpenID Connect</a>, <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/protocols/oauth2">OAuth 2.0</a>, and <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/protocols/saml">SAML</a>.</p> 
           <p>If you want to implement authentication in your application, it is suggested that you reference our <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/quickstarts">Quickstart Tutorials</a> which walk you through the implementation for a wide range of technologies and platforms.</p> 
           <p>You can make use of the Authentication API by making the HTTP requests yourself or by making use of the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js">Auth0.js library</a>. You can also use the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/lock">Lock widget</a> for web applications, or alternatively you can make use of <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/lock-ios/v2">Lock for iOS</a> and <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/lock-android">Lock for Android</a>.</p> 
           <p>We also have SDKs available for <a href="https://github.com/auth0/Auth0.net">.NET</a>, <a href="https://github.com/auth0/Auth0-java">Java</a>, <a href="https://github.com/auth0/node-auth0">Node</a>, <a href="https://github.com/auth0/auth0-php">PHP</a> and <a href="https://github.com/auth0/auth0-python">Python</a>, or alternatively you can use any middleware in your web applications which supports OpenID Connect or OAuth 2.0.</p> 
           <p>For each endpoint in this document you will find sample snippets you can use, in three available formats:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>HTTP request</li> 
            <li>Curl command</li> 
            <li>JavaScript: depending on the endpoint each snippet may use the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js">Auth0.js library</a>, Node.js code or simple JavaScript</li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
          <div class="api-section" data-section="none"> 
           <h1 id="login" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Login</h1> 
           <h2 id="social" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Social</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">GET https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/authorize?
  response_type=code|token&amp;
  client_id=YOUR_CLIENT_ID&amp;
  connection=CONNECTION&amp;
  redirect_uri=https://YOUR_APP/callback&amp;
  state=STATE&amp;
  additional-parameter=ADDITIONAL_PARAMETERS
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">// Script uses auth0.js v8. See Remarks for details.
&lt;script src="https://cdn.auth0.com/js/auth0/8.9/auth0.min.js"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;
&lt;script type="text/javascript"&gt;
  // Initialize client
  var webAuth = new auth0.WebAuth({
    domain:       'YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN',
    clientID:     'YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
  });
  
  // Trigger login with google
  webAuth.authorize({
    connection: 'google-oauth2'
  });

  // Trigger login with github
  webAuth.authorize({
    connection: 'github'
  });

  // Trigger login popup with twitter
  webAuth.popup.authorize({
    connection: 'twitter'
  });
&lt;/script&gt;
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-primary" href="#social">GET</span> <span class="path" href="#social">/authorize</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>Use this endpoint to authenticate a user with a social provider. It will return a <code>302</code> redirect to the social provider specified in <code>connection</code>.</p> 
           <div class="alert alert-default alert-with-icon"> 
            <i class="icon-budicon-724 alert-icon"></i> 
            <div class="alert-content"> 
             <p>Social connections only support browser-based (passive) authentication because most social providers don't allow a username and password to be entered into applications that they don't own. Therefore, the user will be redirected to the provider's sign in page.</p> 
            </div>
           </div> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>response_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use <code>code</code> for server side flows and <code>token</code> for client side flows</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The <code>client_id</code> of your client</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>connection</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The name of a social identity provider configured to your client, for example <code>google-oauth2</code> or <code>facebook</code>. If null, it will redirect to the <a href="https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/login">Auth0 Login Page</a> and show the Login Widget.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>redirect_uri</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The URL to which Auth0 will redirect the browser after authorization has been granted by the user.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>state</code> <br><span class="label label-primary">Recommended</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">An opaque value the clients adds to the initial request that the authorization server includes when redirecting the back to the client. This value must be used by the client to prevent CSRF attacks.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>additional-parameter</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use this to send additional parameters to the provider. For example, <code>access_type=offline</code> (for Google refresh tokens) , <code>display=popup</code> (for Windows Live popup mode).</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the fields <strong>Client</strong> (select the client you want to use for the test) and <strong>Connection</strong> (the name of the social connection to use).</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, click <strong>OAuth2 / OIDC Login</strong>.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <p>The <code>redirect_uri</code> value must be specified as a valid callback URL under your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client's Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>If <code>response_type=token</code>, after the user authenticates on the provider, it will redirect to your application <code>callback URL</code> passing the <code>access_token</code> and <code>id_token</code> in the address <code>location.hash</code>. This is used for Single Page Apps and also on Native Mobile SDKs.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>The sample auth0.js script uses the library version 8. If you are using auth0.js version 7, please see this <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v7">reference guide</a>.</p> </li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="6" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/identityproviders#social">Supported Social Identity Providers</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/social/oauth2">Custom Social Connections</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/protocols/oauth2/oauth-state">Using the State Parameter</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v8#webauth-authorize-">Auth0.js v8 /authorize Method Reference</a></li> 
           </ul> 
           <h2 id="database-ad-ldap-passive-" class="anchor-heading"><span id="7" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Database/AD/LDAP (Passive)</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">GET https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/authorize?
  response_type=code|token&amp;
  client_id=YOUR_CLIENT_ID&amp;
  connection=CONNECTION&amp;
  redirect_uri=https://YOUR_APP/callback&amp;
  state=STATE
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">// Script uses auth0.js v8. See Remarks for details.
&lt;script src="https://cdn.auth0.com/js/auth0/8.9/auth0.min.js"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;
&lt;script type="text/javascript"&gt;
  // Initialize Client
  var webAuth = new auth0.WebAuth({
    domain:       'YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN',
    clientID:     'YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
  });
  
  // Calculate URL to redirect to
  var url = webAuth.client.buildAuthorizeUrl({
    clientID: 'YOUR_CLIENT_ID', // string
    responseType: 'token', // code or token
    redirectUri: 'https://YOUR_APP/callback',
    state: 'YOUR_STATE'
  });
  
  // Redirect to url
  // ...
&lt;/script&gt;
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-primary" href="#database-ad-ldap-passive-">GET</span> <span class="path" href="#database-ad-ldap-passive-">/authorize</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>Use this endpoint for browser based (passive) authentication. It returns a <code>302</code> redirect to the <a href="https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/login">Auth0 Login Page</a> that will show the Login Widget where the user can login with email and password.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="8" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>response_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use <code>code</code> for server side flows and <code>token</code> for client side flows.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The <code>client_id</code> of your client.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>connection</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The name of the connection configured to your client. If null, it will redirect to the <a href="https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/login">Auth0 Login Page</a> and show the Login Widget using the first database connection.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>redirect_uri</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The URL to which Auth0 will redirect the browser after authorization has been granted by the user.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>state</code> <br><span class="label label-primary">Recommended</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">An opaque value the clients adds to the initial request that the authorization server includes when redirecting the back to the client. This value must be used by the client to prevent CSRF attacks.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="9" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the fields <strong>Client</strong> (select the client you want to use for the test) and <strong>Connection</strong> (the name of the social connection to use).</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, click <strong>OAuth2 / OIDC Login</strong>.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="10" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>The <code>redirect_uri</code> value must be specified as a valid callback URL under your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client's Settings</a>.</li> 
            <li>If <code>response_type=token</code>, after the user authenticates, it will redirect to your application <code>callback URL</code> passing the <code>access_token</code> and <code>id_token</code> in the address <code>location.hash</code>. This is used for Single Page Apps and also on Native Mobile SDKs.</li> 
            <li>The main difference between passive and active authentication is that the former happens in the browser through the <a href="https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/login">Auth0 Login Page</a> and the latter can be invoked from anywhere (a script, server to server, and so forth).</li> 
            <li>The sample auth0.js script uses the library version 8. If you are using auth0.js version 7, please see this <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v7">reference guide</a>.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="11" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/database">Database Identity Providers</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/database/rate-limits">Rate Limits on User/Password Authentication</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connector">Active Directory/LDAP Connector</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/protocols/oauth2/oauth-state">Using the State Parameter</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v8#webauth-authorize-">Auth0.js v8 /authorize Method Reference</a></li> 
           </ul> 
           <h2 id="enterprise-saml-and-others-" class="anchor-heading"><span id="12" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Enterprise (SAML and Others)</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">GET https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/authorize?
  response_type=code|token&amp;
  client_id=YOUR_CLIENT_ID&amp;
  connection=CONNECTION&amp;
  redirect_uri=https://YOUR_APP/callback&amp;
  state=STATE
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">// Script uses auth0.js v8. See Remarks for details.
&lt;script src="https://cdn.auth0.com/js/auth0/8.9/auth0.min.js"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;
&lt;script type="text/javascript"&gt;
  // Initialize client
  var webAuth = new auth0.WebAuth({
    domain:       'YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN',
    clientID:     'YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
  });
  
  // Trigger login using redirect with credentials to enterprise connections 
  webAuth.redirect.loginWithCredentials({
    connection: 'Username-Password-Authentication',
    username: 'testuser',
    password: 'testpass',
    scope: 'openid'
  });

  // Trigger login using popup mode with credentials to enterprise connections
  webAuth.popup.loginWithCredentials({
    connection: 'Username-Password-Authentication',
    username: 'testuser',
    password: 'testpass',
    scope: 'openid'
  });
&lt;/script&gt;
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-primary" href="#enterprise-saml-and-others-">GET</span> <span class="path" href="#enterprise-saml-and-others-">/authorize</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>Use this endpoint for passive authentication. It returns a <code>302</code> redirect to the SAML Provider (or Windows Azure AD and the rest, as specified in the <code>connection</code>) to enter their credentials.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="13" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>response_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use <code>code</code> for server side flows, <code>token</code> for client side flows.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The <code>client_id</code> of your client.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>connection</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The name of the connection configured to your client. If null, it will redirect to the <a href="https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/login">Auth0 Login Page</a> and show the Login Widget using the first database connection.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>redirect_uri</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The URL to which Auth0 will redirect the browser after authorization has been granted by the user.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>state</code> <br><span class="label label-primary">Recommended</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">An opaque value the clients adds to the initial request that the authorization server includes when redirecting the back to the client. This value must be used by the client to prevent CSRF attacks.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="14" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the fields <strong>Client</strong> (select the client you want to use for the test) and <strong>Connection</strong> (the name of the social connection to use).</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, click <strong>OAuth2 / OIDC Login</strong>.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="15" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>If no <code>connection</code> is specified, it will redirect to the <a href="https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/login">Login Page</a> and show the Login Widget.</li> 
            <li>The <code>redirect_uri</code> value must be specified as a valid callback URL under your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client's Settings</a>.</li> 
            <li>If <code>response_type=token</code>, after the user authenticates, it will redirect to your application <code>callback URL</code> passing the <code>access_token</code> and <code>id_token</code> in the address <code>location.hash</code>. This is used for Single Page Apps and also on Native Mobile SDKs.</li> 
            <li>Additional parameters can be sent that will be passed to the provider.</li> 
            <li>The sample auth0.js script uses the library version 8. If you are using auth0.js version 7, please see this <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v7">reference guide</a>.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="16" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/protocols/saml">SAML</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/enterprise/azure-active-directory">Obtain a ClientId and Client Secret for Microsoft Azure Active Directory</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/protocols/oauth2/oauth-state">Using the State Parameter</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v8#webauth-authorize-">Auth0.js v8 /authorize Method Reference</a></li> 
           </ul> 
          </div>

           <h1 id="logout" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Logout</h1> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">GET https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/v2/logout?
  client_id=YOUR_CLIENT_ID&amp;
  returnTo=LOGOUT_URL
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request GET \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/v2/logout' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"client_id":"YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "returnTo":"LOGOUT_URL"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">// Script uses auth0.js v8. See Remarks for details.
&lt;script src="https://cdn.auth0.com/js/auth0/8.9/auth0.min.js"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;
&lt;script type="text/javascript"&gt;
  // Initialize client
  var webAuth = new auth0.WebAuth({
    domain:       'YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN',
    clientID:     'YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
  });
  
  webAuth.logout({
    returnTo: 'YOUR_LOGOUT_URL',
    client_id: 'YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
  });
&lt;/script&gt;
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-primary" href="#logout">GET</span> <span class="path" href="#logout">/v2/logout</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>Use this endpoint to logout a user. If you want to navigate the user to a specific URL after the logout, set that URL at the <code>returnTo</code> parameter. The URL should be included in any the appropriate <code>Allowed Logout URLs</code> list:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>If the <code>client_id</code> parameter is included, the <code>returnTo</code> URL must be listed in the <code>Allowed Logout URLs</code> set at the client level (see <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/logout#set-the-allowed-logout-urls-at-the-client-level">Setting Allowed Logout URLs at the App Level</a>).</li> 
            <li>If the <code>client_id</code> parameter is NOT included, the <code>returnTo</code> URL must be listed in the <code>Allowed Logout URLs</code> set at the tenant level (see <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/logout#set-the-allowed-logout-urls-at-the-tenant-level">Setting Allowed Logout URLs at the Tenant Level</a>).</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>returnTo</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">URL to redirect the user after the logout.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The <code>client_id</code> of your client.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>federated</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Add this querystring parameter to the logout URL, to log the user out of their identity provider, as well: <code>https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/v2/logout?federated</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the fields <strong>Client</strong> (select the client you want to use for the test) and <strong>Connection</strong> (the name of the social connection to use).</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Logout URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Other Flows</em> tab, click <strong>Logout</strong>, or <strong>Logout (Federated)</strong> to log the user out of the identity provider as well.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>Logging the user out of their identity provider is not common practice, so think about the user experience before you use the <code>federated</code> querystring parameter.</li> 
            <li>The sample auth0.js script uses the library version 8. If you are using auth0.js version 7, please see this <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v7">reference guide</a>.</li> 
           </ul>

           </ul>

           <h1 id="passwordless" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Passwordless</h1> 
           <p>Passwordless connections do not require the user to remember a password. Instead, another mechanism is used to prove identity, such as a one-time code sent through email or SMS, every time the user logs in.</p> 
           <h2 id="get-code-or-link" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Get Code or Link</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/passwordless/start
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "connection": "email|sms",
  "email": "EMAIL", //set for connection=email
  "phone_number": "PHONE_NUMBER", //set for connection=sms
  "send": "link|code", //if left null defaults to link
  "authParams": { // any authentication parameters that you would like to add
    "scope": "openid",
    "state": "YOUR_STATE"
  }
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/passwordless/start' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"client_id":"YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "connection":"email|sms", "email":"EMAIL", "phone_number":"PHONE_NUMBER", "send":"link|code", "authParams":{"scope": "openid","state": "YOUR_STATE"}}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">// Script uses auth0.js v8. See Remarks for details.
&lt;script src="https://cdn.auth0.com/js/auth0/8.9/auth0.min.js"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;
&lt;script type="text/javascript"&gt;
  // Initialize client
  var webAuth = new auth0.WebAuth({
    domain:       'YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN',
    clientID:     'YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
  });

  // Send a verification code using email
  webAuth.passwordlessStart({
      connection: 'email',
      send: 'code',
      email: 'USER_EMAIL'
    }, function (err,res) {
      // handle errors or continue
    }
  );

  // Send a link using email
  webAuth.passwordlessStart({
      connection: 'email',
      send: 'link',
      email: 'USER_EMAIL'
    }, function (err,res) {
      // handle errors or continue
    }
  );

  // Send a verification code using SMS
  webAuth.passwordlessStart({
      connection: 'sms',
      send: 'code',
      phoneNumber: 'USER_PHONE_NUMBER'
    }, function (err,res) {
      // handle errors or continue
    }
  );
&lt;/script&gt;
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#get-code-or-link">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#get-code-or-link">/passwordless/start</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>You have three options for <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/passwordless">passwordless authentication</a>:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>Send a verification code using email.</li> 
            <li>Send a link using email.</li> 
            <li>Send a verification code using SMS.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The <code>client_id</code> of your client.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>connection</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">How to send the code/link to the user. Use <code>email</code> to send the code/link using email, or <code>sms</code> to use SMS.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>email</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Set this to the user's email address, when <code>connection=email</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>phone_number</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Set this to the user's phone number, when <code>connection=sms</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>send</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use <code>link</code> to send a link or <code>code</code> to send a verification code. If null, a link will be sent.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>authParams</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use this to append or override the link parameters (like <code>scope</code>, <code>redirect_uri</code>, <code>protocol</code>, <code>response_type</code>), when you send a link using email.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-postman" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Postman</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can test this endpoint using <a href="https://www.getpostman.com/">Postman</a>. We have a preconfigured collection that you can download and use. Simply click the button below. For more info refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/postman">Using the Auth0 API with our Postman Collections</a>.</p> 
           <p> <a href="https://app.getpostman.com/run-collection/608670c820cda215594c"> <img src="https://run.pstmn.io/button.svg" alt="Run in Postman"> </a> </p> 
           <p></p> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>If you sent a verification code, using either email or SMS, after you get the code, you have to authenticate the user using the <a href="#authenticate-user">/oauth/ro endpoint</a>, using <code>email</code> or <code>phone_number</code> as the <code>username</code>, and the verification code as the <code>password</code>.</li> 
            <li>The sample auth0.js script uses the library version 8. If you are using auth0.js version 7, please see this <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v7">reference guide</a>.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="error-codes" class="anchor-heading"><span id="6" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Error Codes</h3> 
           <p>For the complete error code reference for this endpoint refer to <a href="#post-passwordless-start">Errors &gt; POST /passwordless/start</a>.</p> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="7" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/passwordless">Passwordless Authentication</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/passwordless/email">Authenticate users with using Passwordless Authentication via Email</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/passwordless/sms">Authenticate users with a one-time code via SMS</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/passwordless/ios-touch-id-swift">Authenticate users with Touch ID</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/passwordless/faq">Passwordless FAQ</a></li> 
           </ul> 
           <h2 id="authenticate-user" class="anchor-heading"><span id="8" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Authenticate User</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/ro
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "connection": "email|sms",
  "grant_type": "password",
  "username": "EMAIL|PHONE", //email or phone number
  "password": "VERIFICATION_CODE", //the verification code
  "scope": "SCOPE"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/ro' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"client_id":"YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "connection":"email|sms", "grant_type":"password", "username":"EMAIL|PHONE", "password":"VERIFICATION_CODE", "scope":"SCOPE"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">// Script uses auth0.js v8. See Remarks for details.
&lt;script src="https://cdn.auth0.com/js/auth0/8.9/auth0.min.js"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;
&lt;script type="text/javascript"&gt;
  // Initialize client
  var webAuth = new auth0.WebAuth({
    domain:       'YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN',
    clientID:     'YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
  });

  // Verify code sent via email
  webAuth.passwordlessVerify({
      connection: 'email',
      email: 'USER_EMAIL',
      verificationCode: 'VERIFICATION_CODE_SENT'
    }, function (err,res) {
      // handle errors or continue
    }
  );

  // Verify code sent within link using email
  webAuth.passwordlessVerify({
      connection: 'email',
      email: 'USER_EMAIL',
      verificationCode: 'VERIFICATION_CODE_SENT_WITHIN_LINK'
    }, function (err,res) {
      // handle errors or continue
    }
  );

  // Verify code sent via SMS
  webAuth.passwordlessVerify({
      connection: 'sms',
      phoneNumber: 'USER_PHONE_NUMBER',
      verificationCode: 'VERIFICATION_CODE_SENT'
    }, function (err,res) {
      // handle errors or continue
    }
  );
&lt;/script&gt;
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#authenticate-user">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#authenticate-user">/oauth/ro</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <div class="alert alert-warning alert-with-icon"> 
            <i class="icon-budicon-354 alert-icon"></i> 
            <div class="alert-content"> 
             <p>This feature is disabled by default for new tenants as of 8 June 2017. Please see <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/clients/client-grant-types">Client Grant Types</a> for more information.</p> 
            </div>
           </div> 
           <p>Once you have a verification code, use this endpoint to login the user with their phone number/email and verification code. This is active authentication, so the user must enter the code in your app.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="9" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The <code>client_id</code> of your client.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>connection</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use <code>sms</code> or <code>email</code> (should be the same as <a href="#get-code-or-link">POST /passwordless/start</a>)</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>grant_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use <code>password</code></td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>username</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The user's phone number if <code>connection=sms</code>, or the user's email if <code>connection=email</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>password</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The user's verification code.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>scope</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use <code>openid</code> to get an <code>id_token</code>, or <code>openid profile email</code> to include also user profile information in the <code>id_token</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table>

           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="11" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the fields <strong>Client</strong> (select the client you want to use for the test) and <strong>Connection</strong> (use <code>sms</code> or <code>email</code>).</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, set <strong>Username</strong> to the user's phone number if <code>connection=sms</code>, or the user's email if <code>connection=email</code>, and <strong>Password</strong> to the user's verification code. Click <strong>Resource Owner Endpoint</strong>.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="12" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>The <code>profile</code> scope value requests access to the End-User's default profile Claims, which are: <code>name</code>, <code>family_name</code>, <code>given_name</code>, <code>middle_name</code>, <code>nickname</code>, <code>preferred_username</code>, <code>profile</code>, <code>picture</code>, <code>website</code>, <code>gender</code>, <code>birthdate</code>, <code>zoneinfo</code>, <code>locale</code>, and <code>updated_at</code>.</li> 
            <li>The <code>email</code> scope value requests access to the <code>email</code> and <code>email_verified</code> Claims.</li> 
            <li>The sample auth0.js script uses the library version 8. If you are using auth0.js version 7, please see this <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v7">reference guide</a>.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="error-codes" class="anchor-heading"><span id="13" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Error Codes</h3> 
           <p>For the complete error code reference for this endpoint refer to <a href="#post-oauth-ro">Errors &gt; POST /oauth/ro</a>.</p>

           <h1 id="signup" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Signup</h1> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/dbconnections/signup
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "email": "EMAIL",
  "password": "PASSWORD",
  "connection": "CONNECTION",
  "user_metadata": { plan: 'silver', team_id: 'a111' }
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/dbconnections/signup' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"client_id":"YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "email":"EMAIL", "password":"PASSWORD", "connection":"CONNECTION", "user_metadata":"{ plan: 'silver', team_id: 'a111' }"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">// Script uses auth0.js v8. See Remarks for details.
&lt;script src="https://cdn.auth0.com/js/auth0/8.9/auth0.min.js"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;
&lt;script type="text/javascript"&gt;
  // Initialize client
  var webAuth = new auth0.WebAuth({
    domain:       'YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN',
    clientID:     'YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
  });
  
  webAuth.signup({ 
    connection: 'CONNECTION', 
    email: 'EMAIL', 
    password: 'PASSWORD',
    user_metadata: { plan: 'silver', team_id: 'a111' }
  }, function (err) { 
    if (err) return alert('Something went wrong: ' + err.message); 
      return alert('success signup without login!') 
  });
&lt;/script&gt;
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-json">{
  "_id": "58457fe6b27...",
  "email_verified": false,
  "email": "test.account@signup.com"
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#signup">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#signup">/dbconnections/signup</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>Given a user's credentials, and a <code>connection</code>, this endpoint will create a new user using active authentication.</p> 
           <p>This endpoint only works for database connections.</p>

           <h1 id="change-password" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Change Password</h1> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/dbconnections/change_password
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "email": "EMAIL",
  "password": "",
  "connection": "CONNECTION",
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/dbconnections/change_password \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID","email": "EMAIL", "password": "", "connection": "CONNECTION"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">// Script uses auth0.js v8. See Remarks for details.

&lt;script type="text/javascript"&gt;
  var webAuth = new auth0.WebAuth({
    domain:       'YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN',
    clientID:     'YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
  });
  
  webAuth.changePassword({
    connection: 'CONNECTION',
    email:   'EMAIL'
  }, function (err, resp) {
    if(err){
      console.log(err.message);
    }else{
      console.log(resp);
    }
  });
&lt;/script&gt;
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#change-password">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#change-password">/dbconnections/change_password</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">"We've just sent you an email to reset your password."
</code></pre> 
           <p>Given a user's <code>email</code> address and a <code>connection</code>, Auth0 will send a change password email.</p> 
           <p>This endpoint only works for database connections.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The <code>client_id</code> of your client.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>email</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The user's email address.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>password</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The new password. See the next paragraph for the case when a password can be set.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>connection</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The name of the database connection configured to your client.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-postman" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Postman</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can test this endpoint using <a href="https://www.getpostman.com/">Postman</a>. We have a preconfigured collection that you can download and use. Simply click the button below. For more info refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/postman">Using the Auth0 API with our Postman Collections</a>.</p> 
           <p> <a href="https://app.getpostman.com/run-collection/608670c820cda215594c"> <img src="https://run.pstmn.io/button.svg" alt="Run in Postman"> </a> </p> 
           <p></p> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>If you are using Lock version 9 and above, <strong>do not set the password field</strong> or you will receive a <em>password is not allowed</em> error. You can only set the password if you are using Lock version 8.</li> 
            <li>If a password is provided, when the user clicks on the confirm password change link, the new password specified in this POST will be set for this user.</li> 
            <li>If a password is NOT provided, when the user clicks on the password change link they will be redirected to a page asking them for a new password.</li> 
            <li>The sample auth0.js script uses the library version 8. If you are using auth0.js version 7, please see this <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v7">reference guide</a>.</li> 
            <li>This endpoint will return three HTTP Response Headers, that provide relevant data on its rate limits: 
             <ul> 
              <li><code>X-RateLimit-Limit</code>: Number of requests allowed per minute.</li> 
              <li><code>X-RateLimit-Remaining</code>: Number of requests available. Each new request reduces this number by 1. For each minute that passes, requests are added back, so this number increases by 1 each time.</li> 
              <li><code>X-RateLimit-Reset</code>: Remaining time until the rate limit (<code>X-RateLimit-Limit</code>) resets. The value is in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unix_time">UTC epoch seconds</a>.</li> 
             </ul> </li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/database/password-change">Changing a User's Password</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/database/password-strength">Password Strength in Auth0 Database Connections</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/database/password-options">Password Options in Auth0 Database Connections</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/policies/rate-limits">Auth0 API Rate Limit Policy</a></li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
          <div class="api-section" data-section="none"> 
           <h1 id="user-profile" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>User Profile</h1> 
           <h2 id="get-user-info" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Get User Info</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">GET https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/userinfo
Authorization: 'Bearer {ACCESS_TOKEN}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request GET \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/userinfo' \
  --header 'authorization: Bearer {ACCESS_TOKEN}' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">// Script uses auth0.js v8. See Remarks for details.
&lt;script src="https://cdn.auth0.com/js/auth0/8.9/auth0.min.js"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;
&lt;script type="text/javascript"&gt;
  // Initialize the Auth0 client
  var webAuth = new auth0.WebAuth({
    domain:       'YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN',
    clientID:     'YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
  });
  
  // Parse the URL and extract the access_token
  webAuth.parseHash(window.location.hash, function(err, authResult) {
    if (err) {
      return console.log(err);
    }
    webAuth.client.userInfo(authResult.accessToken, function(err, user) {
        // This method will make a request to the /userinfo endpoint 
        // and return the user object, which contains the user's information, 
        // similar to the response below.
    });
  });
&lt;/script&gt;
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-json">{
  "email_verified": false,
  "email": "test.account@userinfo.com",
  "clientID": "q2hnj2iu...",
  "updated_at": "2016-12-05T15:15:40.545Z",
  "name": "test.account@userinfo.com",
  "picture": "https://s.gravatar.com/avatar/dummy.png",
  "user_id": "auth0|58454...",
  "nickname": "test.account",
  "created_at": "2016-12-05T11:16:59.640Z",
  "sub": "auth0|58454..."
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-primary" href="#get-user-info">GET</span> <span class="path" href="#get-user-info">/userinfo</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>Given the Auth0 <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/tokens/access-token">access token</a> obtained during login, this endpoint returns a user's profile.</p> 
           <p>This endpoint will work only if <code>openid</code> was granted as a scope for the <code>access_token</code>.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>access_token</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The Auth0 <code>access_token</code> obtained during login.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-postman" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Postman</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can test this endpoint using <a href="https://www.getpostman.com/">Postman</a>. We have a preconfigured collection that you can download and use. Simply click the button below. For more info refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/postman">Using the Auth0 API with our Postman Collections</a>.</p> 
           <p> <a href="https://app.getpostman.com/run-collection/608670c820cda215594c"> <img src="https://run.pstmn.io/button.svg" alt="Run in Postman"> </a> </p> 
           <p></p> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>The sample auth0.js script uses the library version 8. If you are using auth0.js version 7, please see this <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v7">reference guide</a>.</li> 
            <li>The auth0.js <code>parseHash</code> method, requires that your tokens are signed with <code>RS256</code>, rather than <code>HS256</code>. For more information about this, check the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/migration-guide#the-parsehash-method">Auth0.js v8 Migration Guide</a>.</li> 
            <li>If you want this endpoint to return <code>user_metadata</code> or other custom information, you can use <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/rules#api-authorization-add-claims-to-access-tokens">rules</a>. For more information refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/adoption/scope-custom-claims">User profile claims and scope</a>.</li> 
            <li>This endpoint will return three HTTP Response Headers, that provide relevant data on its rate limits: 
             <ul> 
              <li><code>X-RateLimit-Limit</code>: Number of requests allowed per minute.</li> 
              <li><code>X-RateLimit-Remaining</code>: Number of requests available. Each new request reduces this number by 1. For each minute that passes, requests are added back, so this number increases by 1 each time.</li> 
              <li><code>X-RateLimit-Reset</code>: Remaining time until the rate limit (<code>X-RateLimit-Limit</code>) resets. The value is in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unix_time">UTC epoch seconds</a>.</li> 
             </ul> </li> 
            <li>The <code>Email</code> claim returns a snapshot of the email at the time of login</li> 
            <li>Standard claims (other than <code>email</code>) return the latest value (unless the value comes from an external IdP)</li> 
            <li>Custom claims return a snapshot of the value at the time of login</li> 
            <li>To access the most up-to-date values for the <code>email</code> or custom claims, you must get new tokens. You can log in using silent authentication (where the <code>prompt</code> parameter for your call to the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/authentication#authorization-code-grant"><code>authorize</code> endpoint</a> equals <code>none</code>)</li> 
            <li>To access the most up-to-date values for standard claims that were changed using an external IdP (for example, the user changed their email address in Facebook)., you must get new tokens. Log in again using the external IdP, but <em>not</em> with silent authentication.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="6" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <p><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js#extract-the-authresult-and-get-user-info">Auth0.js v8 Reference: Extract the authResult and get user info</a></p> </li> 
            <li> <p><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/policies/rate-limits">Auth0 API Rate Limit Policy</a></p> </li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
          <div class="api-section" data-section="none"> 
           <h1 id="saml" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>SAML</h1> 
           <p>The SAML protocol is used for 3rd party SaaS applications mostly, like Salesforce and Box. Auth0 supports SP and IDP Initiated Sign On. For more information refer to: <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/protocols/saml">SAML</a>.</p> 
           <h2 id="accept-request" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Accept Request</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">GET https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/samlp/YOUR_CLIENT_ID?
  connection=CONNECTION
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request GET \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/samlp/YOUR_CLIENT_ID' \
  --header 'content-type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded' \
  --data '"connection"="CONNECTION"'
</code></pre> 
           <p> </p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-primary" href="#accept-request">GET</span> <span class="path" href="#accept-request">/samlp/YOUR_CLIENT_ID</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>Use this endpoint to accept a SAML request to initiate a login.</p> 
           <p>Optionally, it accepts a connection parameter to login with a specific provider. If no connection is specified, the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/login_page">Auth0 Login Page</a> will be shown.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The <code>client_id</code> of your client.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>connection</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The connection to use.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-postman" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Postman</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can test this endpoint using <a href="https://www.getpostman.com/">Postman</a>. We have a preconfigured collection that you can download and use. Simply click the button below. For more info refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/postman">Using the Auth0 API with our Postman Collections</a>.</p> 
           <p> <a href="https://app.getpostman.com/run-collection/608670c820cda215594c"> <img src="https://run.pstmn.io/button.svg" alt="Run in Postman"> </a> </p> 
           <p></p> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>All the parameters of the SAML response can be modified with <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/rules">Rules</a>.</li> 
            <li>The SAML request <code>AssertionConsumerServiceURL</code> will be used to <code>POST</code> back the assertion. It must match the application's <code>callback_URL</code>.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="6" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/protocols/saml">SAML</a></li> 
           </ul> 
           <h2 id="get-metadata" class="anchor-heading"><span id="7" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Get Metadata</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">GET https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/samlp/metadata/YOUR_CLIENT_ID
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request GET \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/samlp/metadata/YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
</code></pre> 
           <p> </p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-primary" href="#get-metadata">GET</span> <span class="path" href="#get-metadata">/samlp/metadata/YOUR_CLIENT_ID</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>This endpoint returns the SAML 2.0 metadata.</p>

           <h2 id="idp-initiated-sso-flow" class="anchor-heading"><span id="11" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>IdP-Initiated SSO Flow</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/login/callback?connection=CONNECTION
Content-Type: 'application/x-www-form-urlencoded'
  SAMLResponse=SAML_RESPONSE
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/login/callback' \
  --header 'content-type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded' \
  --data '"connection":"CONNECTION", "SAMLResponse":"SAML_RESPONSE"'
</code></pre> 
           <p> </p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#idp-initiated-sso-flow">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#idp-initiated-sso-flow">/login/callback</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>This endpoint accepts an IdP-Initiated Sign On SAMLResponse from a SAML Identity Provider. The connection corresponding to the identity provider is specified in the querystring. The user will be redirected to the application that is specified in the SAML Provider IdP-Initiated Sign On section.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="12" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>connection</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The name of an identity provider configured to your client.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>SAMLResponse</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">An IdP-Initiated Sign On SAML Response.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="13" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the field <strong>Client</strong> (select the client you want to use for the test) and <strong>Connection</strong> (the name of the configured identity provider).</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Other Flows</em> tab, click <strong>SAML</strong>.</p> </li> 
           </ol>
