           <h1 id="ws-federation" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>WS-Federation</h1> 
           <h2 id="accept-request" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Accept Request</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">GET https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/wsfed/YOUR_CLIENT_ID
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request GET \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/wsfed/YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
</code></pre> 
           <p> </p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-primary" href="#accept-request20">GET</span> <span class="path" href="#accept-request20">/wsfed/YOUR_CLIENT_ID</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>This endpoint accepts a WS-Federation request to initiate a login.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client-id</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The <code>client-id</code> of your client.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>wtrealm</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Can be used in place of <code>client-id</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>whr</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The name of the connection (used to skip the login page).</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>wctx</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's state.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>wreply</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The callback URL.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-postman" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Postman</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can test this endpoint using <a href="https://www.getpostman.com/">Postman</a>. We have a preconfigured collection that you can download and use. Simply click the button below. For more info refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/postman">Using the Auth0 API with our Postman Collections</a>.</p> 
           <p> <a href="https://app.getpostman.com/run-collection/608670c820cda215594c"> <img src="https://run.pstmn.io/button.svg" alt="Run in Postman"> </a> </p> 
           <p></p> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the field <strong>Client</strong> (select the client you want to use for the test) and <strong>Connection</strong> (the name of the configured identity provider).</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Other Flows</em> tab, click <strong>WS-Federation</strong>.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="6" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>The <code>wtrealm</code> parameter must be in one of these formats: 
             <ul> 
              <li><code>urn:clientID</code> (e.g. urn:YOUR_CLIENT_ID)</li> 
              <li>If this parameter does not begin with a urn, the <code>client.clientAliases</code> array is used for look-up. This can only be set with the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/management/v2#!/Clients/get_clients">/api/v2/clients</a> Management API.</li> 
             </ul> </li> 
            <li>The <code>whr</code> parameter is mapped to the connection like this: <code>urn:CONNECTION_NAME</code>. For example, <code>urn:google-oauth2</code> indicates login with Google. If there is no <code>whr</code> parameter included, the user will be directed to the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/login_page">Auth0 Login Page</a>.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="7" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/protocols/ws-fed">WS-Federation</a></li> 
           </ul>

           <p></p> 
           <p>This endpoint returns the WS-Federation metadata.</p>

           <h1 id="account-linking" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Account Linking</h1> 
           <h2 id="link" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Link</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">GET https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/authorize?
  response_type=code|token&amp;
  client_id=YOUR_CLIENT_ID&amp;
  connection=CONNECTION&amp;
  redirect_uri=https://YOUR_APP/callback&amp;
  access_token=LOGGED_IN_USER_ACCESS_TOKEN
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-primary" href="#link">GET</span> <span class="path" href="#link">/authorize</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <div class="alert alert-warning alert-with-icon"> 
            <i class="icon-budicon-354 alert-icon"></i> 
            <div class="alert-content"> 
             <p>This endpoint is <strong>deprecated</strong> for account linking. The <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/management/v2#!/Users/post_identities">POST /api/v2/users/{id}/identities</a> should be used instead. For more information refer to the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/migrations#account-linking-removal">Migration Notice</a>.</p> 
            </div>
           </div> 
           <p>Call this endpoint when a user wants to link a second authentication method (for example, a user/password database connection, with Facebook).</p> 
           <p>This endpoint will trigger the login flow to link an existing account with a new one. This will return a 302 redirect to the <code>connection</code> that the current user wants to add. The user is identified by the <code>access_token</code> that was returned on login success.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>response_type</code><br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use <code>code</code> for server side flows, <code>token</code> for client side flows</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code><br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The <code>client_id</code> of your client</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>connection</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The name of the connection configured to your client. If null, it will redirect to <a href="https://auth0.com/#/login_page">Auth0 Login Page</a> and show the Login Widget using the first database connection.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>redirect_uri</code><br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The URL to which Auth0 will redirect the browser after authorization has been granted by the user.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>access_token</code><br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The logged-in user's access token</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>The <code>redirect_uri</code> value must be specified as a valid callback URL under your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client's Settings</a>.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3>

           <h2 id="unlink" class="anchor-heading"><span id="6" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Unlink</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/login/unlink
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "access_token": "LOGGED_IN_USER_ACCESS_TOKEN", // Primary identity access_token
  "user_id": "LINKED_USER_ID" // (provider|id)
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/login/unlink' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"access_token": "LOGGED_IN_USER_ACCESS_TOKEN", "user_id": "LINKED_USER_ID"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var url = 'https://' + YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN + '/login/unlink';
var params = 'access_token=LOGGED_IN_USER_ACCESS_TOKEN&amp;user_id=' + localStorage.getItem('user_id');

var xhr = new XMLHttpRequest();
xhr.open('POST', url);
xhr.setRequestHeader('Content-Type', 'application/json');

xhr.onload = function() {
  if (xhr.status == 200) {
    fetchProfile();
  } else {
    alert("Request failed: " + xhr.statusText);
  }
};

xhr.send(params);
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#unlink">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#unlink">/login/unlink</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <div class="alert alert-warning alert-with-icon"> 
            <i class="icon-budicon-354 alert-icon"></i> 
            <div class="alert-content"> 
             <p>This endpoint is <strong>deprecated</strong>. The <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/management/v2#!/Users/delete_provider_by_user_id">DELETE /api/v2/users/{id}/identities/{provider}/{user_id}</a> should be used instead.</p> 
            </div>
           </div> 
           <p>Given a logged-in user's <code>access_token</code> and <code>user_id</code>, this endpoint will unlink a user's account from the identity provider.</p>

           <h1 id="impersonation" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Impersonation</h1> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/users/{user_id}/impersonate
Content-Type:   'application/json'
Authorization:  'Bearer {ACCESS_TOKEN}'
{
  protocol: "PROTOCOL",
  impersonator_id: "IMPERSONATOR_ID",
  client_id: "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  additionalParameters: [
    "response_type": "code",
    "state": "STATE"
  ]
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/users/{user_id}/impersonate' \
  --header 'Authorization: Bearer {ACCESS_TOKEN}' \
  --header 'content-type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded; charset=UTF-8' \
  --data '{"protocol":"PROTOCOL", "impersonator_id":"IMPERSONATOR_ID", "client_id":"YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "additionalParameters": {"response_type": "code", "state": "STATE"}}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var url = 'https://' + YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN + '/users/' + localStorage.getItem('user_id') + '/impersonate';
var params = 'protocol=PROTOCOL&amp;impersonator_id=IMPERSONATOR_ID&amp;client_id=YOUR_CLIENT_ID';

var xhr = new XMLHttpRequest();

xhr.open('POST', url);
xhr.setRequestHeader('Content-Type', 'application/json');
xhr.setRequestHeader('Authorization', 'Bearer ' + localStorage.getItem('access_token'));

xhr.onload = function() {
  if (xhr.status == 200) {
    fetchProfile();
  } else {
    alert("Request failed: " + xhr.statusText);
  }
};

xhr.send(params);
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-text">https:/YOUR_DOMAIN/users/IMPERSONATOR_ID/impersonate?&amp;bewit=WFh0MUtm...
</code></pre> 
           <p> </p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#impersonation">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#impersonation">/users/{user_id}/impersonate</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <div class="alert alert-warning alert-with-icon"> 
            <i class="icon-budicon-354 alert-icon"></i> 
            <div class="alert-content"> 
             <p>Impersonation functionality may be disabled by default for your tenant. To check, go to the <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/users">Users</a> page in the Dashboard, select a user, and see if the <strong>Sign in as User</strong> button is displayed. If you can't see it, <a href="https://support.auth0.com">contact support</a> and ask them to enable the feature for your tenant.</p> 
            </div>
           </div> 
           <p>Use this endpoint to obtain an impersonation URL to login as another user. Useful for troubleshooting.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>protocol</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The protocol to use against the identity provider: <code>oauth2</code>, <code>samlp</code>, <code>wsfed</code>, <code>wsfed-rms</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>impersonator_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td>

             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>additionalParameters</code></td>

           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <p>This endpoint can only be used with <strong>Global Client</strong> credentials.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>To distinguish between real logins and impersonation logins, the profile of the impersonated user will contain additional impersonated and impersonator properties. For example: <code>"impersonated": true, "impersonator": {"user_id": "auth0|...", "email": "admin@example.com"}</code>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>For a regular web app, you should set the <code>additionalParameters</code>: set the <code>response_type</code> to be <code>code</code>, the <code>callback_url</code> to be the callback url to which Auth0 will redirect with the authorization code, and the <code>scope</code> to be the JWT claims that you want included in the JWT.</p> </li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/user-profile/user-impersonation">Impersonation</a></li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
          <p><span data-section-label="api-authz">API Authorization</span></p> 
          <div class="api-section" data-section="api-authz"> 
           <h1 id="authorize-client" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Authorize Client</h1> 
           <p>To begin an OAuth 2.0 Authorization flow, your Client application should first send the user to the authorization URL.</p> 
           <p>The purpose of this call is to obtain consent from the user to invoke the API (specified in <code>audience</code>) and do certain things (specified in <code>scope</code>) on behalf of the user. Auth0 will authenticate the user and obtain consent, unless consent has been previously given. If you alter the value in <code>scope</code>, Auth0 will require consent to be given again.</p> 
           <p>The OAuth 2.0 flows that require user authorization are:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/authorization-code">Authorization Code Grant</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/authorization-code-pkce">Authorization Code Grant using Proof Key for Code Exchange (PKCE)</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/implicit">Implicit Grant</a></li> 
           </ul> 
           <p>On the other hand, the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/password">Resource Owner Password Grant</a> and <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/client-credentials">Client Credentials</a> flows do not use this endpoint since there is no user authorization involved. Instead they invoke directly the <code>POST /oauth/token</code> endpoint to retrieve an access token.</p> 
           <p>Based on the OAuth 2.0 flow you are implementing, the parameters slightly change. To determine which flow is best suited for your case refer to: <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/which-oauth-flow-to-use">Which OAuth 2.0 flow should I use?</a>.</p> 
           <h2 id="authorization-code-grant" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Authorization Code Grant</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">GET https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/authorize?
  audience=API_IDENTIFIER&amp;
  scope=SCOPE&amp;
  response_type=code&amp;
  client_id=YOUR_CLIENT_ID&amp;
  redirect_uri=https://YOUR_APP/callback&amp;
  state=STATE
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-text">HTTP/1.1 302 Found
Location: https://YOUR_APP/callback?code=AUTHORIZATION_CODE&amp;state=STATE
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-primary" href="#authorization-code-grant">GET</span> <span class="path" href="#authorization-code-grant">/authorize</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>This is the OAuth 2.0 grant that regular web apps utilize in order to access an API.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>audience</code> <br></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The unique identifier of the target API you want to access.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>scope</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The scopes which you want to request authorization for. These must be separated by a space. You can request any of the <a href="https://openid.net/specs/openid-connect-core-1_0.html#StandardClaims">standard OIDC scopes</a> about users, such as <code>profile</code> and <code>email</code>, custom claims that must <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/adoption/scope-custom-claims">conform to a namespaced format</a>, or any scopes supported by the target API (for example, <code>read:contacts</code>). Include <code>offline_access</code> to get a refresh token.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>response_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Indicates to Auth0 which OAuth 2.0 flow you want to perform. Use <code>code</code> for Authorization Code Grant Flow.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client ID.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>state</code> <br><span class="label label-primary">Recommended</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">An opaque value the clients adds to the initial request that Auth0 includes when redirecting the back to the client. This value must be used by the client to prevent CSRF attacks.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>redirect_uri</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The URL to which Auth0 will redirect the browser after authorization has been granted by the user.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>prompt</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">To initiate a <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/silent-authentication">silent authentication</a> request, use <code>prompt=none</code> (see Remarks for more info).</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the <strong>Client</strong> field to the client you want to use for the test.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, set the fields <strong>Audience</strong> (to the unique identifier of the API you want to access), <strong>Response Type</strong> (set to <code>code</code>) and enable the <strong>Audience</strong> switch.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Click <strong>OAuth / OIDC Login</strong>. Following the redirect, the URL will contain the authorization code. Note, that the code will be set at the <strong>Authorization Code</strong> field so you can proceed with exchanging it for an access token.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>In order to improve compatibility for client applications, Auth0 will now return profile information in a <a href="https://openid.net/specs/openid-connect-core-1_0.html#StandardClaims">structured claim format as defined by the OIDC specification</a>. This means that in order to add custom claims to ID tokens or access tokens, they must conform to a namespaced format to avoid possible collisions with standard OIDC claims. For example, if you choose the namespace <code>https://foo.com/</code> and you want to add a custom claim named <code>myclaim</code>, you would name the claim <code>https://foo.com/myclaim</code>, instead of <code>myclaim</code>.</li> 
            <li>Include <code>offline_access</code> to the <code>scope</code> request parameter to get a refresh token from <a href="#authorization-code">POST /oauth/token</a>. Make sure that the <strong>Allow Offline Access</strong> field is enabled in the <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/apis">API Settings</a>.</li> 
            <li>The <code>redirect_uri</code> value must be specified as a valid callback URL under your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client's Settings</a>.</li> 
            <li>Silent authentication lets you perform an authentication flow where Auth0 will only reply with redirects, and never with a login page. When an access token has expired, silent authentication can be used to retrieve a new one without user interaction, assuming the user's SSO session has not expired.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="6" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/authorization-code">Calling APIs from Server-side Web Apps</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/authorization-code-grant">Executing an Authorization Code Grant Flow</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/protocols/oauth2/oauth-state">Using the State Parameter</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/silent-authentication">Silent Authentication</a></li> 
           </ul> 
           <h2 id="authorization-code-grant-pkce-" class="anchor-heading"><span id="7" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Authorization Code Grant (PKCE)</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">GET https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/authorize?
  audience=API_IDENTIFIER&amp;
  scope=SCOPE&amp;
  response_type=code&amp;
  client_id=YOUR_CLIENT_ID&amp;
  redirect_uri=https://YOUR_APP/callback&amp;
  code_challenge=CODE_CHALLENGE&amp;
  code_challenge_method=S256
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-text">HTTP/1.1 302 Found
Location: https://YOUR_APP/callback?code=AUTHORIZATION_CODE
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-primary" href="#authorization-code-grant-pkce-">GET</span> <span class="path" href="#authorization-code-grant-pkce-">/authorize</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>This is the OAuth 2.0 grant that mobile apps utilize in order to access an API. Before starting with this flow, you need to generate and store a <code>code_verifier</code>, and using that, generate a <code>code_challenge</code> that will be sent in the authorization request.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="8" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>audience</code> <br></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The unique identifier of the target API you want to access.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>scope</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The scopes which you want to request authorization for. These must be separated by a space. You can request any of the <a href="https://openid.net/specs/openid-connect-core-1_0.html#StandardClaims">standard OIDC scopes</a> about users, such as <code>profile</code> and <code>email</code>, custom claims that must conform to a namespaced format, or any scopes supported by the target API (for example, <code>read:contacts</code>). Include <code>offline_access</code> to get a refresh token.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>response_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Indicates to Auth0 which OAuth 2.0 Flow you want to perform. Use <code>code</code> for Authorization Code Grant (PKCE) Flow.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client ID.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>state</code> <br><span class="label label-primary">Recommended</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">An opaque value the clients adds to the initial request that Auth0 includes when redirecting the back to the client. This value must be used by the client to prevent CSRF attacks.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>redirect_uri</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The URL to which Auth0 will redirect the browser after authorization has been granted by the user.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>code_challenge_method</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Method used to generate the challenge. The PKCE spec defines two methods, <code>S256</code> and <code>plain</code>, however, Auth0 supports only <code>S256</code> since the latter is discouraged.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>code_challenge</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Generated challenge from the <code>code_verifier</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>prompt</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">To initiate a <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/silent-authentication">silent authentication</a> request, use <code>prompt=none</code> (see Remarks for more info).</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="9" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the <strong>Client</strong> field to the client you want to use for the test.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, set the fields <strong>Audience</strong> (to the unique identifier of the API you want to access), <strong>Response Type</strong> (set to <code>code</code>) and enable the <strong>Audience</strong> and <strong>PKCE</strong> switches.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Click <strong>OAuth / OIDC Login</strong>. Following the redirect, the URL will contain the authorization code. Note, that the code will be set at the <strong>Authorization Code</strong> field, and the <strong>Code Verifier</strong> will be automatically set as well, so you can proceed with exchanging the code for an access token.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="10" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>In order to improve compatibility for client applications, Auth0 will now return profile information in a <a href="https://openid.net/specs/openid-connect-core-1_0.html#StandardClaims">structured claim format as defined by the OIDC specification</a>. This means that in order to add custom claims to ID tokens or access tokens, they must conform to a namespaced format to avoid possible collisions with standard OIDC claims. For example, if you choose the namespace <code>https://foo.com/</code> and you want to add a custom claim named <code>myclaim</code>, you would name the claim <code>https://foo.com/myclaim</code>, instead of <code>myclaim</code>.</li> 
            <li>Include <code>offline_access</code> to the <code>scope</code> request parameter to get a refresh token from <a href="#authorization-code-pkce-">POST /oauth/token</a>. Make sure that the <strong>Allow Offline Access</strong> field is enabled in the <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/apis">API Settings</a>.</li> 
            <li>The <code>redirect_uri</code> value must be specified as a valid callback URL under your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client's Settings</a>.</li> 
            <li>Silent authentication lets you perform an authentication flow where Auth0 will only reply with redirects, and never with a login page. When an access token has expired, silent authentication can be used to retrieve a new one without user interaction, assuming the user's SSO session has not expired.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="11" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/authorization-code-pkce">Calling APIs from Mobile Apps</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/authorization-code-grant-pkce">Executing an Authorization Code Grant Flow with PKCE</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/silent-authentication">Silent Authentication</a></li> 
           </ul> 
           <h2 id="implicit-grant" class="anchor-heading"><span id="12" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Implicit Grant</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">GET https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/authorize?
  audience=API_IDENTIFIER&amp;
  scope=SCOPE&amp;
  response_type=token|id_token|id_token token&amp;
  client_id=YOUR_CLIENT_ID&amp;
  redirect_uri=https://YOUR_APP/callback&amp;
  state=STATE&amp;
  nonce=NONCE
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-text">HTTP/1.1 302 Found
Location: https://YOUR_APP/callback#access_token=TOKEN&amp;state=STATE&amp;token_type=TYPE&amp;expires_in=SECONDS
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-primary" href="#implicit-grant">GET</span> <span class="path" href="#implicit-grant">/authorize</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>This is the OAuth 2.0 grant that Client-side web apps utilize in order to access an API.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="13" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>audience</code> <br></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The unique identifier of the target API you want to access.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>scope</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The scopes which you want to request authorization for. These must be separated by a space. You can request any of the <a href="https://openid.net/specs/openid-connect-core-1_0.html#StandardClaims">standard OIDC scopes</a> about users, such as <code>profile</code> and <code>email</code>, custom claims that must conform to a namespaced format, or any scopes supported by the target API (for example, <code>read:contacts</code>).</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>response_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">This will specify the type of token you will receive at the end of the flow. Use <code>token</code> to get only an <code>access_token</code>, <code>id_token</code> to get only an <code>id_token</code> (if you don't plan on accessing an API), or <code>id_token token</code> to get both an <code>id_token</code> and an <code>access_token</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client ID.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>state</code> <br><span class="label label-primary">Recommended</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">An opaque value the clients adds to the initial request that Auth0 includes when redirecting the back to the client. This value must be used by the client to prevent CSRF attacks.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>redirect_uri</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The URL to which Auth0 will redirect the browser after authorization has been granted by the user.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>nonce</code> <br><span class="label label-primary">Recommended</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">A string value which will be included in the ID token response from Auth0, <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/nonce">used to prevent token replay attacks</a>. It is required for <code>response_type=id_token token</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>connection</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The name of the connection configured to your client.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>prompt</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">To initiate a <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/silent-authentication">silent authentication</a> request, use <code>prompt=none</code> (see Remarks for more info).</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="14" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3>

           </div>

           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="15" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>The <code>redirect_uri</code> value must be specified as a valid callback URL under your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client's Settings</a>.</li> 
            <li>If <code>response_type=token</code>, after the user authenticates with the provider, this will redirect them to your application callback URL while passing the <code>access_token</code> in the address <code>location.hash</code>. This is used for Single Page Apps and on Native Mobile SDKs.</li> 
            <li>The Implicit Grant does not support the issuance of refresh tokens. You can use <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/silent-authentication">Silent Authentication</a> instead.</li> 
            <li>In order to improve compatibility for client applications, Auth0 will now return profile information in a <a href="https://openid.net/specs/openid-connect-core-1_0.html#StandardClaims">structured claim format as defined by the OIDC specification</a>. This means that in order to add custom claims to ID tokens or access tokens, they must conform to a namespaced format to avoid possible collisions with standard OIDC claims. For example, if you choose the namespace <code>https://foo.com/</code> and you want to add a custom claim named <code>myclaim</code>, you would name the claim <code>https://foo.com/myclaim</code>, instead of <code>myclaim</code>.</li> 
            <li>Silent authentication lets you perform an authentication flow where Auth0 will only reply with redirects, and never with a login page. When an access token has expired, silent authentication can be used to retrieve a new one without user interaction, assuming the user's SSO session has not expired.</li> 
           </ul>

          <div class="api-section" data-section="api-authz"> 
           <h1 id="get-token" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Get Token</h1> 
           <p>Use this endpoint to:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>Get an <code>access_token</code> in order to call an API. You can, optionally, retrieve an <code>id_token</code> and a <code>refresh_token</code> as well.</li> 
            <li>Refresh your access token, using a refresh token you got during authorization.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <p>Note that the only OAuth 2.0 flows that can retrieve a refresh token are:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/authorization-code">Authorization Code</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/authorization-code-pkce">Authorization Code with PKCE</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/password">Resource Owner Password</a></li> 
           </ul> 
           <h2 id="authorization-code" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Authorization Code</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "grant_type": "authorization_code",
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET",
  "code": "AUTHORIZATION_CODE",
  "redirect_uri": https://YOUR_APP/callback
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"grant_type":"authorization_code","client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID","client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET","code": "AUTHORIZATION_CODE","redirect_uri": "https://YOUR_APP/callback"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var request = require("request");

var options = { method: 'POST',
  url: 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token',
  headers: { 'content-type': 'application/json' },
  body:
   { grant_type: 'authorization_code',
     client_id: 'YOUR_CLIENT_ID',
     client_secret: 'YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET',
     code: 'AUTHORIZATION_CODE',
     redirect_uri: 'https://YOUR_APP/callback' },
  json: true };

request(options, function (error, response, body) {
  if (error) throw new Error(error);

  console.log(body);
});
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
{
  "access_token":"eyJz93a...k4laUWw",
  "refresh_token":"GEbRxBN...edjnXbL",
  "id_token":"eyJ0XAi...4faeEoQ",
  "token_type":"Bearer",
  "expires_in":86400
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#authorization-code">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#authorization-code">/oauth/token</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>This is the OAuth 2.0 grant that regular web apps utilize in order to access an API. Use this endpoint to exchange an Authorization Code for a Token.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>grant_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Denotes the flow you are using. For Authorization Code use <code>authorization_code</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client ID.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_secret</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client Secret.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>code</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The Authorization Code received from the initial <code>/authorize</code> call.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>redirect_uri</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">This is required only if it was set at the <a href="#authorization-code-grant">GET /authorize</a> endpoint. The values must match.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-postman" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Postman</h3>

For more info refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/postman">Using the Auth0 API with our Postman Collections</a>.</p> 
           <p> <a href="https://app.getpostman.com/run-collection/608670c820cda215594c"> <img src="https://run.pstmn.io/button.svg" alt="Run in Postman"> </a> </p>

           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <p>If you have just executed the <a href="#authorization-code-grant">Authorization Code Grant</a> you should already have a code set at the <strong>Authorization Code</strong> field of the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab. If so, click <strong>OAuth2 Code Exchange</strong>, otherwise follow the instructions.</p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the <strong>Client</strong> field to the client you want to use for the test.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, set the field <strong>Authorization Code</strong> to the code you retrieved from <a href="#authorization-code-grant">Authorization Code Grant</a>. Click <strong>OAuth2 Code Exchange</strong>.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="6" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/authorization-code">Calling APIs from Server-side Web Apps</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/authorization-code-grant">Executing an Authorization Code Grant Flow</a></li> 
           </ul> 
           <h2 id="authorization-code-pkce-" class="anchor-heading"><span id="7" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Authorization Code (PKCE)</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "grant_type": "authorization_code",
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "code_verifier": "CODE_VERIFIER",
  "code": "AUTHORIZATION_CODE",
  "redirect_uri": "com.myclientapp://myclientapp.com/callback"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"grant_type":"authorization_code","client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID","code_verifier": "CODE_VERIFIER","code": "AUTHORIZATION_CODE","redirect_uri": "com.myclientapp://myclientapp.com/callback"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var request = require("request");

var options = { method: 'POST',
  url: 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token',
  headers: { 'content-type': 'application/json' },
  body: '{"grant_type":"authorization_code","client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID","code_verifier": "CODE_VERIFIER","code": "AUTHORIZATION_CODE","redirect_uri": "com.myclientapp://myclientapp.com/callback", }' };

request(options, function (error, response, body) {
  if (error) throw new Error(error);

  console.log(body);
});
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
{
  "access_token":"eyJz93a...k4laUWw",
  "refresh_token":"GEbRxBN...edjnXbL",
  "id_token":"eyJ0XAi...4faeEoQ",
  "token_type":"Bearer",
  "expires_in":86400
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#authorization-code-pkce-">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#authorization-code-pkce-">/oauth/token</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>This is the OAuth 2.0 grant that mobile apps utilize in order to access an API. Use this endpoint to exchange an Authorization Code for a Token.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="8" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>grant_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Denotes the flow you are using. For Authorization Code (PKCE) use <code>authorization_code</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client ID.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>code</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The Authorization Code received from the initial <code>/authorize</code> call.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>code_verifier</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Cryptographically random key that was used to generate the <code>code_challenge</code> passed to <code>/authorize</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>redirect_uri</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">This is required only if it was set at the <a href="#authorization-code-grant-pkce-">GET /authorize</a> endpoint. The values must match.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="9" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <p>If you have just executed the <a href="#authorization-code-grant-pkce-">Authorization Code Grant (PKCE)</a> you should already have the <strong>Authorization Code</strong> and <strong>Code Verifier</strong> fields, of the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, set. If so, click <strong>OAuth2 Code Exchange</strong>, otherwise follow the instructions.</p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the <strong>Client</strong> field to the client you want to use for the test.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, set the field <strong>Authorization Code</strong> to the code you retrieved from <a href="#authorization-code-grant-pkce-">Authorization Code Grant</a>, and the <strong>Code Verifier</strong> to the key. Click <strong>OAuth2 Code Exchange</strong>.</p> </li> 
           </ol>

           <h2 id="client-credentials" class="anchor-heading"><span id="11" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Client Credentials</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  audience: "API_IDENTIFIER",
  grant_type: "client_credentials",
  client_id: "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  client_secret: "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"audience":"API_IDENTIFIER", "grant_type":"client_credentials", "client_id":"YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "client_secret":"YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var request = require("request");

var options = { method: 'POST',
  url: 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token',
  headers: { 'content-type': 'application/json' },
  body:
   { client_id: 'YOUR_CLIENT_ID',
     client_secret: 'YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET',
     audience: 'API_IDENTIFIER',
     grant_type: 'client_credentials' },
  json: true };

request(options, function (error, response, body) {
  if (error) throw new Error(error);

  console.log(body);
});
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
{
  "access_token":"eyJz93a...k4laUWw",
  "token_type":"Bearer",
  "expires_in":86400
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#client-credentials">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#client-credentials">/oauth/token</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>This is the OAuth 2.0 grant that server processes utilize in order to access an API. Use this endpoint to directly request an <code>access_token</code> by using the Client Credentials (a Client Id and a Client Secret).</p>
