           <h2 id="resource-owner-password" class="anchor-heading"><span id="15" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Resource Owner Password</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "grant_type": "password",
  "username": "USERNAME",
  "password": "PASSWORD",
  "audience": "API_IDENTIFIER",
  "scope": "SCOPE",
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"grant_type":"password", "username":"USERNAME", "password":"PASSWORD", "audience":"API_IDENTIFIER", "scope":"SCOPE", "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET"
 }'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var request = require("request");

var options = { method: 'POST',
  url: 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token',
  headers: { 'content-type': 'application/json' },
  body:
   { grant_type: 'password',
     username: 'USERNAME',
     password: 'PASSWORD',
     audience: 'API_IDENTIFIER',
     scope: 'SCOPE',
     client_id: 'YOUR_CLIENT_ID',
     client_secret: 'YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET' },
  json: true };

request(options, function (error, response, body) {
  if (error) throw new Error(error);

  console.log(body);
});
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
{
  "access_token":"eyJz93a...k4laUWw",
  "token_type":"Bearer",
  "expires_in":86400
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#resource-owner-password">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#resource-owner-password">/oauth/token</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>This is the OAuth 2.0 grant that highly trusted apps utilize in order to access an API. In this flow the end-user is asked to fill in credentials (username/password) typically using an interactive form in the user-agent (browser). This information is later on sent to the client and Auth0. It is therefore imperative that the client is absolutely trusted with this information.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="16" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>grant_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Denotes the flow you are using. For Resource Owner Password use <code>password</code>. To add realm support use <code>http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/password-realm</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client ID.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_secret</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client Secret. <strong>Required</strong> when the <strong>Token Endpoint Authentication Method</strong> field at your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a> is <code>Post</code> or <code>Basic</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>audience</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The unique identifier of the target API you want to access.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>username</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Resource Owner's identifier.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>password</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Resource Owner's secret.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>scope</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">String value of the different scopes the client is asking for. Multiple scopes are separated with whitespace.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>realm</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">String value of the realm the user belongs. Set this if you want to add realm support at this grant. For more information on what realms are refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/password#realm-support">Realm Support</a>.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="request-headers" class="anchor-heading"><span id="17" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request headers</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>auth0-forwarded-for</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">End-user IP as a string value. Set this if you want brute-force protection to work in server-side scenarios. For more information on how and when to use this header, refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/using-resource-owner-password-from-server-side">Using resource owner password from server-side</a>.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="18" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the <strong>Client</strong> field to the client you want to use for the test.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, set the <strong>Username</strong> and <strong>Password</strong>, and click <strong>Password Grant</strong>.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="19" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>The scopes issued to the client may differ from the scopes requested. In this case, a <code>scope</code> parameter will be included in the response JSON.</li> 
            <li>If you don't request specific scopes, all scopes defined for the audience will be returned due to the implied trust to the client in this grant. You can customize the scopes returned in a rule. For more information, refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/password">Calling APIs from Highly Trusted Clients</a>.</li> 
            <li>To add realm support set the <code>grant_type</code> to <code>http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/password-realm</code>, and the <code>realm</code> to the realm the user belongs. This maps to a connection in Auth0. For example, if you have configured a database connection for your internal employees and you have named the connection <code>employees</code>, then use this value. For more information on how to implement this refer to: <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/password-grant#realm-support">Realm Support</a>.</li> 
            <li>In addition to username and password, Auth0 may also require the end-user to provide an additional factor as proof of identity before issuing the requested scopes. In this case, the request described above will return an <code>mfa_required</code> error along with an <code>mfa_token</code>. You can use these tokens to request a challenge for the possession factor and validate it accordingly. For details refer to <a href="#resource-owner-password-and-mfa">Resource Owner Password and MFA</a>.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="20" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/password">Calling APIs from Highly Trusted Clients</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/password-grant">Executing the Resource Owner Password Grant</a></li> 
           </ul> 
           <h2 id="resource-owner-password-and-mfa" class="anchor-heading"><span id="21" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Resource Owner Password and MFA</h2> 
           <p>In addition to username and password, you may also ask your users to provide an additional factor as proof of identity before issuing the requested tokens.</p> 
           <p>The first step, is to request a challenge based on the challenge types supported by the Client application and the end-user (see next paragraph). This is an optional step, since it is not required if you already know that <code>otp</code> is supported.</p> 
           <p>Next, you have to verify the MFA, using the <code>/oauth/token</code> endpoint and the challenge type specified in the first step: an OTP code, a recovery code, or an OOB challenge.</p> 
           <h3 id="mfa-challenge-request" class="anchor-heading"><span id="22" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>MFA Challenge Request</h3> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/mfa/challenge
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET",
  "mfa_token": "MFA_TOKEN",
  "challenge_type": "oob|otp"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/mfa/challenge' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"mfa_token":"MFA_TOKEN", "challenge_type":"oob otp", "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var request = require("request");

var options = { method: 'POST',
  url: 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/mfa/challenge',
  headers: { 'content-type': 'application/json' },
  body:
   { mfa_token: 'MFA_TOKEN',
     challenge_type: 'oob otp',
     client_id: 'YOUR_CLIENT_ID',
     client_secret: 'YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET' },
  json: true };

request(options, function (error, response, body) {
  if (error) throw new Error(error);

  console.log(body);
});
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE FOR OTP:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
{
  "challenge_type":"otp",
}
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE FOR OOB WITHOUT BINDING METHOD:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
{
  "challenge_type":"oob",
  "oob_code": "abcde...dasg"
}
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE FOR OOB WITH BINDING METHOD:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
{
  "challenge_type":"oob",
  "binding_method":"prompt",
  "oob_code": "abcde...dasg"
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#resource-owner-password-and-mfa">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#resource-owner-password-and-mfa">/mfa/challenge</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>This endpoint lets you request a challenge based on the challenge types supported by the Client application and the end user. The challenge type indicates the channel or mechanism on which to get the challenge and thus prove possession.</p> 
           <p>For details on the supported challenge types refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/multifactor-resource-owner-password">Multifactor Authentication and Resource Owner Password</a>.</p> 
           <h4 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="23" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h4> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>mfa_token</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Token got together with <code>mfa_required</code> error for Resource Owner Password flow.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client ID.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_secret</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client Secret. <strong>Required</strong> when the <strong>Token Endpoint Authentication Method</strong> field at your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a> is <code>Post</code> or <code>Basic</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>challenge_type</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">A whitespace-separated list of the challenges types accepted by your application. Accepted challenge types are <code>oob</code> or <code>otp</code>. Excluding this parameter means that your client application accepts all supported challenge types.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h4 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="24" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h4> 
           <ul> 
            <li>If you already know that <code>otp</code> is supported by the end-user and you don't want to request a different factor, you can skip this step an go directly to <strong>Verify MFA using OTP</strong> below.</li> 
            <li>This mechanism does not support enrollment, the end-user must be enrolled with the preferred method before being able to execute this flow. Otherwise, you will get a <code>unsupported_challenge_type</code> error.</li> 
            <li>Auth0 will choose the challenge type based on the types the end user is enrolled with and the ones that the app supports. If your app does not support any of the challenge types the user has enrolled with, an <code>unsupported_challenge_type</code> error will be returned.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h4 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="25" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h4> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/tutorials/multifactor-resource-owner-password">Multifactor Authentication and Resource Owner Password</a></li> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/multifactor-authentication">Multifactor Authentication in Auth0</a></li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="verify-mfa-using-otp" class="anchor-heading"><span id="26" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Verify MFA using OTP</h3> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET",
  "mfa_token": "MFA_TOKEN",
  "grant_type": "grant_type=http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-otp",
  "otp": "OTP_CODE"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"mfa_token":"MFA_TOKEN", "otp":"OTP_CODE", "grant_type": "grant_type=http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-otp", "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var request = require("request");

var options = { method: 'POST',
  url: 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token',
  headers: { 'content-type': 'application/json' },
  body:
   { mfa_token: 'MFA_TOKEN',
     otp: 'OTP_CODE',
     grant_type: 'http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-otp',
     client_id: 'YOUR_CLIENT_ID',
     client_secret: 'YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET' },
  json: true };

request(options, function (error, response, body) {
  if (error) throw new Error(error);

  console.log(body);
});
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE FOR OTP:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
{
  "access_token":"eyJz93a...k4laUWw",
  "token_type":"Bearer",
  "expires_in":86400
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#resource-owner-password-and-mfa">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#resource-owner-password-and-mfa">/oauth/token</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>To verify MFA using an OTP code your app must prompt the user to get the OTP code, and then make a request to <code>/oauth/token</code> with <code>grant_type=http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-otp</code> including the collected OTP code and the <code>mfa_token</code> you received as part of <code>mfa_required</code> error. The response is going to be the same as the one for <code>password</code> or <code>http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/password-realm</code> grant types.</p> 
           <h4 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="27" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h4> 
           <table class="table">

             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr>

             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>grant_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Denotes the flow you are using. For OTP MFA use <code>http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-otp</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client ID.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_secret</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client Secret. <strong>Required</strong> when the <strong>Token Endpoint Authentication Method</strong> field at your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a> is <code>Post</code> or <code>Basic</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>mfa_token</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The mfa token you received from <code>mfa_required</code> error.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>otp</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td>

             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="verify-mfa-using-an-oob-challenge" class="anchor-heading"><span id="28" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Verify MFA using an OOB challenge</h3> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET",
  "mfa_token": "MFA_TOKEN",
  "grant_type": "grant_type=http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-oob",
  "oob_code": "OOB_CODE",
  "binding_code": "BINDING_CODE"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"mfa_token":"MFA_TOKEN", "oob_code": "OOB_CODE", "binding_code": "BINDING_CODE", "grant_type": "grant_type=http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-oob", "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var request = require("request");

var options = { method: 'POST',
  url: 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token',
  headers: { 'content-type': 'application/json' },
  body:
   { mfa_token: 'MFA_TOKEN',
     oob_code: "OOB_CODE",
     binding_code: "BINDING_CODE"
     grant_type: 'http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-oob',
     client_id: 'YOUR_CLIENT_ID',
     client_secret: 'YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET' },
  json: true };

request(options, function (error, response, body) {
  if (error) throw new Error(error);

  console.log(body);
});
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE FOR PENDING CHALLENGE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
{
  "error":"authorization_pending",
  "error_description":"Authorization pending: please repeat the request in a few seconds."
}
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE FOR VERIFIED CHALLENGE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
{
  "access_token":"eyJz93a...k4laUWw",
  "token_type":"Bearer",
  "expires_in":86400
}
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE FOR REJECTED CHALLENGE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
{
  "error":"invalid_grant",
  "error_description":"MFA Authorization rejected."
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#resource-owner-password-and-mfa">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#resource-owner-password-and-mfa">/oauth/token</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>To verify MFA using an OOB challenge (e.g. Push / SMS) your app must make a request to <code>/oauth/token</code> with <code>grant_type=http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-oob</code>. Include the <code>oob_code</code> you received from the challenge response, as well as the <code>mfa_token</code> you received as part of <code>mfa_required</code> error.</p> 
           <p>The response to this request depends on the status of the underlying challenge verification:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>If the challenge has been accepted and verified: it will be the same as for <code>password</code> or <code>http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/password-realm</code> grant types.</li> 
            <li>If the challenge has been rejected, you will get an <code>invalid_grant</code> error, meaning that the challenge was rejected by the user. At this point you should stop polling, as this response is final.</li> 
            <li>If the challenge verification is still pending (meaning it has not been accepted nor rejected) you will get an <code>authorization_pending</code> error, meaning that you must retry the same request a few seconds later. If you request too frequently you will get a <code>slow_down</code> error.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <p>When the challenge response includes a <code>binding_method: prompt</code> your app needs to prompt the user for the <code>binding_code</code> and send it as part of the request. The <code>binding_code</code> is a usually a 6 digit number (similar to an OTP) included as part of the challenge. No <code>binding_code</code> is necessary if the challenge response did not include a <code>binding_method</code>. In this scenario the response will be immediate; you will receive an <code>invalid_grant</code> or an <code>access_token</code> as response.</p> 
           <h4 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="29" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h4> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>grant_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Denotes the flow you are using. For OTP MFA use <code>http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-oob</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client ID.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_secret</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client Secret. <strong>Required</strong> when the <strong>Token Endpoint Authentication Method</strong> field at your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a> is <code>Post</code> or <code>Basic</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>mfa_token</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The mfa token you received from the <code>mfa_required</code> error.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>oob_code</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The oob code received from the challenge request.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>binding_code</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">A code used to bind the side channel (used to deliver the challenge) with the main channel you are using to authenticate. This is usually an OTP-like code delivered as part of the challenge message.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="verify-mfa-using-a-recovery-code" class="anchor-heading"><span id="30" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Verify MFA using a recovery code</h3> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET",
  "mfa_token": "MFA_TOKEN",
  "grant_type": "grant_type=http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-recovery-code",
  "recovery_code": "RECOVERY_CODE"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"mfa_token":"MFA_TOKEN", "recovery_code":"RECOVERY_CODE", "grant_type": "grant_type=http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-recovery-code", "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var request = require("request");

var options = { method: 'POST',
  url: 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token',
  headers: { 'content-type': 'application/json' },
  body:
   { mfa_token: 'MFA_TOKEN',
     recovery_code: 'RECOVERY_CODE',
     grant_type: 'http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-recover-code',
     client_id: 'YOUR_CLIENT_ID',
     client_secret: 'YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET' },
  json: true };

request(options, function (error, response, body) {
  if (error) throw new Error(error);

  console.log(body);
});
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE FOR OTP:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
{
  "access_token":"eyJz93a...k4laUWw",
  "token_type":"Bearer",
  "expires_in":86400,
  "recovery_code": "abcdefg"
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#resource-owner-password-and-mfa">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#resource-owner-password-and-mfa">/oauth/token</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>Some MFA providers (such as Guardian) support using a recovery code to login. This method is supposed to be used to authenticate when the device you enrolled is not available, or you cannot received the challenge or accept it, for instance, due to connectivity issues.</p> 
           <p>To verify MFA using a recovery code your app must prompt the user for the recovery code, and then make a request to <code>oauth/token</code> with <code>grant_type=http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-recovery-code</code>. Include the collected recovery code and the <code>mfa_token</code> from the <code>mfa_required</code> error. If the recovery code is accepted the response will be the same as for <code>password</code> or <code>http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/password-realm</code> grant types. It might also include a <code>recovery_code</code> field, which the Client application must display to the end-user to be stored securely for future use.</p> 
           <h4 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="31" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h4> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>grant_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Denotes the flow you are using. For OTP MFA use <code>http://auth0.com/oauth/grant-type/mfa-otp</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client ID.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_secret</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client Secret. <strong>Required</strong> when the <strong>Token Endpoint Authentication Method</strong> field at your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a> is <code>Post</code> or <code>Basic</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>mfa_token</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The mfa token from the <code>mfa_required</code> error.</td> 
             </tr>

              <td style="text-align:left"><code>recovery_code</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td>

           <h2 id="refresh-token" class="anchor-heading"><span id="32" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Refresh Token</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "grant_type": "refresh_token",
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET",
  "refresh_token": "YOUR_REFRESH_TOKEN"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"grant_type":"refresh_token","client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID","client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET","refresh_token": "YOUR_REFRESH_TOKEN"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var request = require("request");

var options = { method: 'POST',
  url: 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/token',
  headers: { 'content-type': 'application/json' },
  body:
   { grant_type: 'refresh_token',
     client_id: 'YOUR_CLIENT_ID',
     client_secret: 'YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET',
     refresh_token: 'YOUR_REFRESH_TOKEN'},
  json: true };

request(options, function (error, response, body) {
  if (error) throw new Error(error);

  console.log(body);
});
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
Content-Type: application/json
{
  "access_token": "eyJ...MoQ",
  "expires_in": 86400,
  "scope": "openid offline_access",
  "id_token": "eyJ...0NE",
  "token_type": "Bearer"
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#refresh-token">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#refresh-token">/oauth/token</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>Use this endpoint to refresh an access token, using the refresh token you got during authorization.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="33" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>grant_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Denotes the flow you are using. To refresh a token use <code>refresh_token</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client ID.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_secret</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client Secret. <strong>Required</strong> when the <strong>Token Endpoint Authentication Method</strong> field at your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a> is <code>Post</code> or <code>Basic</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>refresh_token</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The refresh token to use.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-this-endpoint" class="anchor-heading"><span id="34" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test this endpoint</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the <strong>Client</strong> field to the client you want to use for the test.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, set the field <strong>Refresh Token</strong> to the refresh token you have. Click <strong>OAuth2 Refresh Token Exchange</strong>.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="35" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/tokens/preview/refresh-token">Refresh Token</a></li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
          <div class="api-section" data-section="api-authz"> 
           <h1 id="revoke-refresh-token" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Revoke Refresh Token</h1> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/revoke
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET",
  "token": "YOUR_REFRESH_TOKEN",
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/revoke' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{ "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "client_secret": "YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET", "token": "YOUR_REFRESH_TOKEN" }'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var request = require("request");

var options = { method: 'POST',
  url: 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/revoke',
  headers: { 'content-type': 'application/json' },
  body: 
   { client_id: 'YOUR_CLIENT_ID',
     client_secret: 'YOUR_CLIENT_SECRET',
     token: 'YOUR_REFRESH_TOKEN' },
  json: true };

request(options, function (error, response, body) {
  if (error) throw new Error(error);

  console.log(body);
});
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">HTTP/1.1 200 OK
(empty-response-body)
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#revoke-refresh-token">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#revoke-refresh-token">/oauth/revoke</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <p>Since refersh tokens never expire, you need to have a way to invalidate them in case they are compromised or you no longer need them. You can do use using this endpoint.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client ID. The client should match the one the refresh token was issued for.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_secret</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client Secret. Required for <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/clients/client-types#confidential-clients">confidential clients</a>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>token</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The refresh token you want to revoke.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>For non-confidential clients that cannot keep the <code>client_secret</code> safe (for example, mobile apps), the endpoint supports passing no <code>client_secret</code> but the client itself must have the property <code>tokenEndpointAuthMethod</code> set to <code>none</code>. You can do this either from the UI (<a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Dashboard &gt; Clients &gt; client Settings</a>) or using the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/management/v2#!/Clients/patch_clients_by_id">Management API</a>.</li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="error-codes" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Error Codes</h3> 
           <p>For the complete error code reference for this endpoint refer to <a href="#post-oauth-revoke">Errors &gt; POST /oauth/revoke</a>.</p> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/tokens/refresh-token">Refresh Token</a></li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
          <p><span data-section-label="legacy">Legacy</span></p> 
          <div class="api-section" data-section="legacy">

           <h1 id="login" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Login</h1> 
           <h2 id="social-with-provider-s-access-token" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Social with Provider's Access Token</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/access_token
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "access_token": "ACCESS_TOKEN",
  "connection": "CONNECTION",
  "scope": "SCOPE"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/access_token' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"client_id":"YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "access_token":"ACCESS_TOKEN", "connection":"CONNECTION", "scope":"SCOPE"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var url = 'https://' + YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN + '/oauth/access_token';
var params = 'client_id=YOUR_CLIENT_ID&amp;access_token={ACCESS_TOKEN}&amp;connection={CONNECTION}&amp;scope={SCOPE}';

var xhr = new XMLHttpRequest();

xhr.open('POST', url);
xhr.setRequestHeader('Content-Type', 'application/json');

xhr.onload = function() {
  if (xhr.status == 200) {
    fetchProfile();
  } else {
    alert("Request failed: " + xhr.statusText);
  }
};

xhr.send(params);
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">{
  "id_token": "eyJ0eXAiOiJKV1Qi...",
  "access_token": "A9CvPwFojaBI...",
  "token_type": "bearer"
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#social-with-provider-s-access-token">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#social-with-provider-s-access-token">/oauth/access_token</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <div class="alert alert-warning alert-with-icon"> 
            <i class="icon-budicon-354 alert-icon"></i> 
            <div class="alert-content"> 
             <p>This endpoint is part of the legacy authentication pipeline. We recommend that you open the browser to do social authentication instead, which is what <a href="https://developers.googleblog.com/2016/08/modernizing-oauth-interactions-in-native-apps.html">Google and Facebook are recommending</a>. For more information on the latest authentication pipeline refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/intro">Introducing OIDC Conformant Authentication</a>.</p> 
             <p>This feature is disabled by default for new tenants as of 8 June 2017. Please see <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/clients/client-grant-types">Client Grant Types</a> for more information.</p> 
            </div>
           </div> 
           <p>Given the social provider's <code>access_token</code> and the <code>connection</code>, this endpoint will authenticate the user with the provider and return a JSON with the <code>access_token</code> and, optionally, an <code>id_token</code>. This endpoint only works for Facebook, Google, Twitter and Weibo.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The <code>client_id</code> of your client.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>access_token</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The social provider's <code>access_token</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>connection</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The name of an identity provider configured to your app.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>scope</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use <code>openid</code> to get an <code>id_token</code>, or <code>openid profile email</code> to include user information in the <code>id_token</code>. If null, only an <code>access_token</code> will be returned.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-postman" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Postman</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can test this endpoint using <a href="https://www.getpostman.com/">Postman</a>. We have a preconfigured collection that you can download and use. Simply click the button below. For more info refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/postman">Using the Auth0 API with our Postman Collections</a>.</p> 
           <p> <a href="https://app.getpostman.com/run-collection/608670c820cda215594c"> <img src="https://run.pstmn.io/button.svg" alt="Run in Postman"> </a> </p> 
           <p></p> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <p>The <code>profile</code> scope value requests access to the End-User's default profile Claims, which are: <code>name</code>, <code>family_name</code>, <code>given_name</code>, <code>middle_name</code>, <code>nickname</code>, <code>preferred_username</code>, <code>profile</code>, <code>picture</code>, <code>website</code>, <code>gender</code>, <code>birthdate</code>, <code>zoneinfo</code>, <code>locale</code>, and <code>updated_at</code>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>The <code>email</code> scope value requests access to the <code>email</code> and <code>email_verified</code> Claims.</p> </li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="error-codes" class="anchor-heading"><span id="6" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Error Codes</h3> 
           <p>For the complete error code reference for this endpoint refer to <a href="#post-oauth-access_token">Errors &gt; POST /oauth/access_token</a>.</p> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="7" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <p><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/tutorials/calling-an-external-idp-api">Call an Identity Provider API</a></p> </li> 
            <li> <p><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/tokens/idp">Identity Provider Access Tokens</a></p> </li> 
            <li> <p><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/tutorials/adding-scopes-for-an-external-idp">Add scopes/permissions to call Identity Provider's APIs</a></p> </li> 
           </ul> 
           <h2 id="database-ad-ldap-active-" class="anchor-heading"><span id="8" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Database/AD/LDAP (Active)</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/ro
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "username": "USERNAME",
  "password": "PASSWORD",
  "connection": "CONNECTION",
  "scope": "openid"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/ro' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"client_id":"YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "username":"USERNAME", "password":"PASSWORD", "connection":"CONNECTION", "scope":"openid"}'

</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">// Script uses auth0.js v8. See Remarks for details.
&lt;script src="https://cdn.auth0.com/js/auth0/8.9/auth0.min.js"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;
&lt;script type="text/javascript"&gt;
  // Initialize client
  var webAuth = new auth0.WebAuth({
    domain:       'YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN',
    clientID:     'YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
  });

  // Trigger login using redirect with credentials to enterprise connections
  webAuth.redirect.loginWithCredentials({
    connection: 'Username-Password-Authentication',
    username: 'testuser',
    password: 'testpass',
    scope: 'openid'
  });

  // Trigger login using popup mode with credentials to enterprise connections
  webAuth.popup.loginWithCredentials({
    connection: 'Username-Password-Authentication',
    username: 'testuser',
    password: 'testpass',
    scope: 'openid'
  });

  // The client.login method allows for non redirect auth using custom database connections, using /oauth/token.
  webAuth.client.login({
    realm: 'tests',
    username: 'testuser',
    password: 'testpass',
    scope: 'openid profile',
    audience: 'urn:test'
  });
&lt;/script&gt;
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#database-ad-ldap-active-">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#database-ad-ldap-active-">/oauth/ro</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <div class="alert alert-warning alert-with-icon"> 
            <i class="icon-budicon-354 alert-icon"></i> 
            <div class="alert-content"> 
             <p>This endpoint is part of the legacy authentication pipeline and has been replaced in favor of the <a href="#resource-owner-password">Password Grant</a>. For more information on the latest authentication pipeline refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/intro">Introducing OIDC Conformant Authentication</a>.</p> 
            </div>
           </div> 
           <p>Use this endpoint for API-based (active) authentication. Given the user credentials and the <code>connection</code> specified, it will do the authentication on the provider and return a JSON with the <code>access_token</code> and <code>id_token</code>.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="9" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The <code>client_id</code> of your client</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>username</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Username/email of the user to login</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>password</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Password of the user to login</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>connection</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The name of the connection to use for login</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>scope</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Set to <code>openid</code> to retrieve also an <code>id_token</code>, leave null to get only an <code>access_token</code></td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>grant_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Set to <code>password</code> to authenticate using username/password or <code>urn:ietf:params:oauth:grant-type:jwt-bearer</code> to authenticate using an <code>id_token</code> (used to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/passwordless/ios-touch-id-swift">Authenticate users with Touch ID</a>)</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>device</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">String value. Required when <code>grant_type</code> is <code>urn:ietf:params:oauth:grant-type:jwt-bearer</code></td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>id_token</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Used to authenticate using a token instead of username/password, in <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/lock-ios/touchid-authentication">Touch ID</a> scenarios. Required when <code>grant_type</code> is <code>urn:ietf:params:oauth:grant-type:jwt-bearer</code></td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-postman" class="anchor-heading"><span id="10" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Postman</h3>

For more info refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/postman">Using the Auth0 API with our Postman Collections</a>.</p> 
           <p> <a href="https://app.getpostman.com/run-collection/608670c820cda215594c"> <img src="https://run.pstmn.io/button.svg" alt="Run in Postman"> </a> </p> 
           <p></p> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="11" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the fields <strong>Client</strong> (select the client you want to use for the test) and <strong>Connection</strong> (the name of the social connection to use).</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, set <strong>Username</strong> and <strong>Password</strong>. Click <strong>Resource Owner Endpoint</strong>.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="12" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <p>This endpoint only works for database connections, passwordless connections, Active Directory/LDAP, Windows Azure AD and ADFS.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>The main difference between passive and active authentication is that the former happens in the browser through the <a href="https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/login">Auth0 Login Page</a> and the latter can be invoked from anywhere (a script, server to server, and so forth).</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>The sample auth0.js script uses the library version 8. If you are using auth0.js version 7, please see this <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v7">reference guide</a>.</p> </li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="error-codes" class="anchor-heading"><span id="13" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Error Codes</h3> 
           <p>For the complete error code reference for this endpoint refer to <a href="#post-oauth-ro">Errors &gt; POST /oauth/ro</a>.</p> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="14" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <p><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/database">Database Identity Providers</a></p> </li> 
            <li> <p><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connections/database/rate-limits">Rate Limits on User/Password Authentication</a></p> </li> 
            <li> <p><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/connector">Active Directory/LDAP Connector</a></p> </li>

           </ul>

           <h1 id="user-profile" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>User Profile</h1> 
           <h2 id="get-token-info" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Get Token Info</h2> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/tokeninfo
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "id_token": "ID_TOKEN"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/tokeninfo' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"id_token":""}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">&lt;script src="https://cdn.auth0.com/js/auth0/8.9/auth0.min.js"&gt;&lt;/script&gt;
&lt;script type="text/javascript"&gt;
  var webAuth = new auth0.WebAuth({
    domain:       'YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN',
    clientID:     'YOUR_CLIENT_ID'
  });
&lt;/script&gt;

webAuth.parseHash(window.location.hash, function(err, authResult) {
  if (err) {
    return console.log(err);
  }

  webAuth.client.userInfo(authResult.accessToken, function(err, user) {
    // Now you have the user's information
  });
});
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-json">{
  "email_verified": false,
  "email": "foo@bar.com",
  "clientID": "q2hnj2iug0...",
  "updated_at": "2016-12-08T14:26:59.923Z",
  "name": "foo@bar.com",
  "picture": "https://s.gravatar.com/avatar/foobar.png",
  "user_id": "auth0|58454...",
  "nickname": "foo.bar",
  "identities": [
    {
      "user_id": "58454...",
      "provider": "auth0",
      "connection": "Username-Password-Authentication",
      "isSocial": false
    }
  ],
  "created_at": "2016-12-05T11:16:59.640Z",
  "global_client_id": "dfas76s..."
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#get-token-info">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#get-token-info">/tokeninfo</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <div class="alert alert-warning alert-with-icon"> 
            <i class="icon-budicon-354 alert-icon"></i> 
            <div class="alert-content"> 
             <p>This endpoint is part of the legacy authentication pipeline and will be disabled for those who use our latest, OIDC conformant, pipeline. We encourage using the <a href="#get-user-info">/userinfo endpoint</a> instead. For more information on the latest authentication pipeline refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/intro">Introducing OIDC Conformant Authentication</a>.</p> 
            </div>
           </div> 
           <p>This endpoint validates a JSON Web Token (signature and expiration) and returns the user information associated with the user id <code>sub</code> property of the token.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>id_token</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The <code>id_token</code> to use.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-postman" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Postman</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can test this endpoint using <a href="https://www.getpostman.com/">Postman</a>. We have a preconfigured collection that you can download and use. Simply click the button below. For more info refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/postman">Using the Auth0 API with our Postman Collections</a>.</p> 
           <p> <a href="https://app.getpostman.com/run-collection/608670c820cda215594c"> <img src="https://run.pstmn.io/button.svg" alt="Run in Postman"> </a> </p> 
           <p></p> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li>This endpoint will return three HTTP Response Headers, that provide relevant data on its rate limits: 
             <ul> 
              <li><code>X-RateLimit-Limit</code>: Number of requests allowed per minute.</li> 
              <li><code>X-RateLimit-Remaining</code>: Number of requests available. Each new request reduces this number by 1. For each minute that passes, requests are added back, so this number increases by 1 each time.</li> 
              <li><code>X-RateLimit-Reset</code>: Remaining time until the rate limit (<code>X-RateLimit-Limit</code>) resets. The value is in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unix_time">UTC epoch seconds</a>.</li> 
             </ul> </li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="6" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <p><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/user-profile/user-profile-details#api">User Profile: In-Depth Details - API</a></p> </li> 
            <li> <p><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/policies/rate-limits">Auth0 API Rate Limit Policy</a></p> </li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
          <div class="api-section" data-section="legacy">
