           <h1 id="delegation" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Delegation</h1> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/delegation
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "grant_type": "urn:ietf:params:oauth:grant-type:jwt-bearer",
  "id_token" or "refresh_token" : "TOKEN",
  "target": "TARGET_CLIENT_ID",
  "scope": "openid",
  "api_type": "API_TYPE"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/delegation' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{"client_id":"YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "grant_type":"urn:ietf:params:oauth:grant-type:jwt-bearer", "id_token|refresh_token":"TOKEN", "target":"TARGET_CLIENT_ID", "scope":"openid", "api_type":"API_TYPE"}'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">// Delegation is not supported in version 8 of auth0.js.
// For a version 7 sample refer to: https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v7#delegation-token-request
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#delegation">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#delegation">/delegation</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <div class="alert alert-warning alert-with-icon"> 
            <i class="icon-budicon-354 alert-icon"></i> 
            <div class="alert-content"> 
             <p>With the latest Auth0 authentication pipeline, this endpoint should not be used to exchange an ID token issued to one client for a new one issued to a different client, or to use a refresh token for a fresh ID token. For more information refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/intro#delegation">Introducing OIDC Conformant Authentication &gt; Delegation</a>.</p> 
             <p>This feature is disabled by default for new tenants as of 8 June 2017. Please see <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/clients/client-grant-types">Client Grant Types</a> for more information.</p> 
            </div>
           </div> 
           <p>A delegation token should be obtained and used when a client program needs to call the API of an Application Addon, such as Firebase or SAP, registered and configured in Auth0, in the same tenant as the calling program.</p> 
           <p>Given an existing token, this endpoint will generate a new token signed with the <code>target</code> client's secret. This is used to flow the identity of the user from the application to an API.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">?he <code>client_id</code> of your client</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>grant_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use <code>urn:ietf:params:oauth:grant-type:jwt-bearer</code></td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>id_token</code> or <code>refresh_token</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The existing token of the user.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>target</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The target <code>client_id</code></td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>scope</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use <code>openid</code> or <code>openid profile email</code></td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>api_type</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The API to be called.</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-postman" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Postman</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can test this endpoint using <a href="https://www.getpostman.com/">Postman</a>. We have a preconfigured collection that you can download and use. Simply click the button below. For more info refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api/postman">Using the Auth0 API with our Postman Collections</a>.</p> 
           <p> <a href="https://app.getpostman.com/run-collection/608670c820cda215594c"> <img src="https://run.pstmn.io/button.svg" alt="Run in Postman"> </a> </p> 
           <p></p> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the <strong>Client</strong> field to the client you want to use for the test.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, set the fields <strong>ID Token</strong>, <strong>Refresh Token</strong> and <strong>Target Client ID</strong>. Click <strong>Delegation</strong>.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <p>The <code>profile</code> scope value requests access to the End-User's default profile Claims, which are: <code>name</code>, <code>family_name</code>, <code>given_name</code>, <code>middle_name</code>, <code>nickname</code>, <code>preferred_username</code>, <code>profile</code>, <code>picture</code>, <code>website</code>, <code>gender</code>, <code>birthdate</code>, <code>zoneinfo</code>, <code>locale</code>, and <code>updated_at</code>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>The <code>email</code> scope value requests access to the <code>email</code> and <code>email_verified</code> Claims.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Delegation is <strong>not supported</strong> in version 8 of <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js">auth0.js</a>. For a sample in version 7 of the library, refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/auth0js/v7#delegation-token-request">Delegation Token Request</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>This endpoint limits up to 10 requests per minute from the same IP address with the same <code>user_id</code>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>This endpoint will return three HTTP Response Headers, that provide relevant data on its rate limits:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li><code>X-RateLimit-Limit</code>: Number of requests allowed per minute.</li> 
              <li><code>X-RateLimit-Remaining</code>: Number of requests available. Each new request reduces this number by 1. For each minute that passes, requests are added back, so this number increases by 1 each time.</li> 
              <li><code>X-RateLimit-Reset</code>: Remaining time until the rate limit (<code>X-RateLimit-Limit</code>) resets. The value is in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unix_time">UTC epoch seconds</a>.</li> 
             </ul> </li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="6" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <p><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/tokens/delegation">Delegation Tokens</a></p> </li> 
            <li> <p><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/policies/rate-limits">Auth0 API Rate Limit Policy</a></p> </li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
          <div class="api-section" data-section="legacy"> 
           <h1 id="resource-owner" class="anchor-heading"><span id="1" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Resource Owner</h1> 
           <h5 class="code-snippet-title">Examples</h5> 
           <pre><code class="language-http">POST https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/ro
Content-Type: 'application/json'
{
  "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID",
  "connection": "CONNECTION",
  "grant_type": "password",
  "username": "USERNAME",
  "password": "PASSWORD",
  "scope": "SCOPE",
  "id_token": "ID_TOKEN",
  "device": "DEVICE"
}
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-shell">curl --request POST \
  --url 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/ro' \
  --header 'accept: application/json' \
  --header 'content-type: application/json' \
  --data '{ "client_id": "YOUR_CLIENT_ID", "connection": "CONNECTION", "grant_type": "password", "username": "USERNAME", "password": "PASSWORD", "scope": "SCOPE", "id_token": "ID_TOKEN", "device": "DEVICE" }'
</code></pre> 
           <pre><code class="language-javascript">var request = require("request");

var options = { method: 'POST',
  url: 'https://YOUR_AUTH0_DOMAIN/oauth/ro',
  headers: { 'content-type': 'application/json', 'accept': 'application/json' },
  body:
   { connection: 'CONNECTION',
     grant_type: 'PASSWORD',
     username: 'USERNAME',
     client_id: 'YOUR_CLIENT_ID',
     password: 'PASSWORD',
     scope: 'SCOPE',
     id_token: 'ID_TOKEN',
     device: 'DEVICE'},
  json: true };

request(options, function (error, response, body) {
  if (error) throw new Error(error);

  console.log(body);
});
</code></pre> 
           <blockquote> 
            <p>RESPONSE SAMPLE:</p> 
           </blockquote> 
           <pre><code class="language-JSON">{
  "access_token": "eyJz93a...",
  "id_token": "eyJ0XAi...",
  "token_type": "Bearer"
}
</code></pre> 
           <p></p>
           <h5 class="http-method-box"> <span class="badge badge-success" href="#resource-owner">POST</span> <span class="path" href="#resource-owner">/oauth/ro</span> </h5>
           <p></p> 
           <div class="alert alert-warning alert-with-icon"> 
            <i class="icon-budicon-354 alert-icon"></i> 
            <div class="alert-content"> 
             <p>This endpoint is part of the legacy authentication pipeline and has been replaced in favor of the <a href="#resource-owner-password">Password Grant</a>. For more information on the latest authentication pipeline refer to <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/intro">Introducing OIDC Conformant Authentication</a>.</p> 
            </div>
           </div> 
           <p>Given the user's credentials, this endpoint will authenticate the user with the provider and return a JSON object with the <code>access_token</code> and an <code>id_token</code>.</p> 
           <h3 id="request-parameters" class="anchor-heading"><span id="2" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Request Parameters</h3> 
           <table class="table">
            <thead> 
             <tr> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Parameter</th> 
              <th style="text-align:left">Description</th> 
             </tr> 
            </thead> 
            <tbody> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>client_id</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Your application's Client ID.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>connection</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The name of the connection configured to your client</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>grant_type</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use the value <code>password</code></td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>username</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The user's username</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>password</code> <br><span class="label label-danger">Required</span></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">The user's password</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>scope</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Use <code>openid</code> to get an <code>id_token</code>, <code>openid profile email</code> to get an <code>id_token</code> and the user profile, or <code>openid offline_access</code> to get an <code>id_token</code> and a <code>refresh_token</code>.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>id_token</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">Used to authenticate using a token instead of username/password, in <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/libraries/lock-ios/touchid-authentication">Touch ID</a> scenarios.</td> 
             </tr> 
             <tr> 
              <td style="text-align:left"><code>device</code></td> 
              <td style="text-align:left">You should set this to a string, if you are requesting a refresh token (<code>scope=offline_access</code>).</td> 
             </tr> 
            </tbody> 
           </table> 
           <h3 id="test-with-authentication-api-debugger" class="anchor-heading"><span id="3" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Test with Authentication API Debugger</h3> 
           <p></p>
           <p>You can use our <strong>Authentication API Debugger</strong> extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger">Authentication API Debugger extension</a>.</p> 
           <p>Click on <strong>Install Debugger</strong> to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <div class="test-endpoint-box"> 
            <a href="https://auth0.com/docs/extensions/authentication-api-debugger" class="btn btn-primary" target="_blank">Install Debugger</a> 
           </div> 
           <p><strong>If you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.</strong></p> 
           <p>The link varies according to your tenant's region: <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.us.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">US West</a>, <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.eu.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Europe Central</a> or <a href="https://YOUR_TENANT.au.webtask.io/auth0-authentication-api-debugger" target="_blank">Australia</a>.</p> 
           <p></p> 
           <ol> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>Configuration</em> tab, set the <strong>Client</strong> field to the client you want to use for the test, and <strong>Connection</strong> to the name of the connection to use.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>Copy the <strong>Callback URL</strong> and set it as part of the <strong>Allowed Callback URLs</strong> of your <a href="https://manage.auth0.com/#/clients/YOUR_CLIENT_ID/settings">Client Settings</a>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>At the <em>OAuth2 / OIDC</em> tab, set the <strong>Username</strong> and <strong>Password</strong>, and click <strong>Resource Owner Endpoint</strong>.</p> </li> 
           </ol> 
           <h3 id="remarks" class="anchor-heading"><span id="4" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Remarks</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <p>This endpoint only works for database connections, passwordless connections, Active Directory/LDAP, Windows Azure AD and ADFS.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>The <code>profile</code> scope value requests access to the End-User's default profile Claims, which are: <code>name</code>, <code>family_name</code>, <code>given_name</code>, <code>middle_name</code>, <code>nickname</code>, <code>preferred_username</code>, <code>profile</code>, <code>picture</code>, <code>website</code>, <code>gender</code>, <code>birthdate</code>, <code>zoneinfo</code>, <code>locale</code>, and <code>updated_at</code>.</p> </li> 
            <li> <p>The <code>email</code> scope value requests access to the <code>email</code> and <code>email_verified</code> Claims.</p> </li> 
           </ul> 
           <h3 id="error-codes" class="anchor-heading"><span id="5" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>Error Codes</h3> 
           <p>For the complete error code reference for this endpoint refer to <a href="#post-oauth-ro">Errors &gt; POST /oauth/ro</a>.</p> 
           <h3 id="more-information" class="anchor-heading"><span id="6" class="anchor" href="#' + anchor + '"><i class="icon icon-budicon-345"></i></span>More Information</h3> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="https://auth0.com/docs/api-auth/grant/password">Calling APIs from Highly Trusted Clients</a></li> 
           </ul> 
          </div>

\u002F OIDC Login\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fol\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"remarks\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"10\" class=\"anchor\" \u003Ccode\u003Eredirect_uri\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E value must be specified as a valid callback URL under your \u003Ca \u003Ccode\u003Eaccess_token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and \u003Ccode\u003Eid_token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E in the address \u003Ccode\u003Elocation.hash\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. This is used for Single Page Apps and also on Native Mobile SDKs.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe main difference between passive and active authentication is that the former happens in the browser through the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002F__AUTH0_NAMESPACE__\u002Flogin\"\u003EAuth0 Login Page\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and the latter can be invoked from anywhere (a script, server to server, and so forth).\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe sample auth0.js script uses the library version 8. id=\"logout\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"1\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon 'https:\u002F\u002F__AUTH0_NAMESPACE__\u002Fv2\u002Flogout' \\\n  --header 'content-type: application\u002Fjson' \\\n  --data '{&quot;client_id&quot;:&quot;__AUTH0_CLIENT_ID__&quot;, &quot;returnTo&quot;:&quot;LOGOUT_URL&quot;}'\n\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fpre\u003E\n\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-javascript\"\u003E\u002F\u002F Script uses auth0.js v8. See Remarks for details.\n&lt;script src=&quot;https:\u002F\u002Fcdn.auth0.com\u002Fjs\u002Fauth0\u002F8.9\u002Fauth0.min.js&quot;&gt;&lt;\u002Fscript&gt;\n&lt;script type=&quot;text\u002Fjavascript&quot;&gt;\n  \u002F\u002F Initialize client\n  var webAuth = new auth0.WebAuth({\n    domain:       '__AUTH0_NAMESPACE__',\n    clientID:     '__AUTH0_CLIENT_ID__'\n  });\n  \n  webAuth.logout({\n    returnTo: 'YOUR_LOGOUT_URL',\n    client_id: '__AUTH0_CLIENT_ID__'\n  });\n&lt;\u002Fscript&gt;\n\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fpre\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ch5 class=\"http-method-box\"\u003E\n  \u003Cspan class=\"badge badge-primary\" href=\"#logout\"\u003EGET\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n  \u003Cspan class=\"path\" href=\"#logout\"\u003E\u002Fv2\u002Flogout\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fh5\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EUse this endpoint to logout a user. If you want to navigate the user to a specific URL after the logout, set that URL at the \u003Ccode\u003EreturnTo\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E parameter. The URL should be included in any the appropriate \u003Ccode\u003EAllowed Logout URLs\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E list:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIf the \u003Ccode\u003Eclient_id\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E parameter is included, the \u003Ccode\u003EreturnTo\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E URL must be listed in the \u003Ccode\u003EAllowed Logout URLs\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E set at the client level (see \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Flogout#set-the-allowed-logout-urls-at-the-client-level\"\u003ESetting Allowed Logout URLs at the App Level\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIf the \u003Ccode\u003Eclient_id\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E parameter is NOT included, the Level\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"request-parameters\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"2\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003ERequest Parameters\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Ctable Each new request reduces this number by 1. For more info refer to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi\u002Fpostman\"\u003EUsing the Auth0 API with our Postman Collections\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\n  \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fapp.getpostman.com\u002Frun-collection\u002F608670c820cda215594c\"\u003E\n    \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Frun.pstmn.io\u002Fbutton.svg\" alt=\"Run in Postman\" \u002F\u003E\n  \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"remarks\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"5\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003ERemarks\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe sample auth0.js script uses the library version 8. If you are using auth0.js version 7, please see this \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Flibraries\u002Fauth0js\u002Fv7\"\u003Ereference guide\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe auth0.js \u003Ccode\u003EparseHash\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E method, requires that your tokens are signed with \u003Ccode\u003ERS256\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, rather than \u003Ccode\u003EHS256\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. For more information about this, check the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Flibraries\u002Fauth0js\u002Fmigration-guide#the-parsehash-method\"\u003EAuth0.js v8 Migration Guide\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIf you want this endpoint to return \u003Ccode\u003Euser_metadata\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E or other custom information, you can use \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Frules#api-authorization-add-claims-to-access-tokens\"\u003Erules\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. For more information refer to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Ftutorials\u002Fadoption\u002Fscope-custom-claims\"\u003EUser profile claims and scope\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThis endpoint will return three HTTP Response Headers, that provide relevant data on its rate limits:\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ccode\u003EX-RateLimit-Limit\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E: Number of requests allowed per minute.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ccode\u003EX-RateLimit-Remaining\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E: Number of requests available. Each new request reduces this number by 1. For each minute that passes, requests are added back, so this number increases by 1 each time.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ccode\u003EX-RateLimit-Reset\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E: Remaining time until the rate limit (\u003Ccode\u003EX-RateLimit-Limit\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E) resets. The value is in \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fen.wikipedia.org\u002Fwiki\u002FUnix_time\"\u003EUTC epoch seconds\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe \u003Ccode\u003EEmail\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E claim returns a snapshot of the email at the time of login\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EStandard claims (other than \u003Ccode\u003Eemail\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E) return the latest value (unless the value comes from an external IdP)\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ECustom claims return a snapshot of the value at the time of login\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ETo access the most up-to-date values for the \u003Ccode\u003Eemail\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E or custom claims, you must get new tokens. You can log in using silent authentication (where the \u003Ccode\u003Eprompt\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E parameter for your call to the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi\u002Fauthentication#authorization-code-grant\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eauthorize\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E endpoint\u003C\u002Fa\u003E equals \u003Ccode\u003Enone\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E)\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ETo access the most up-to-date values for standard claims that were changed using an external IdP (for example, the user changed their email address in Facebook)., you must get new tokens. Log in again using the external IdP, but \u003Cem\u003Enot\u003C\u002Fem\u003E with silent authentication.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"more-information\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"6\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EMore Information\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Flibraries\u002Fauth0js#extract-the-authresult-and-get-user-info\"\u003EAuth0.js v8 Reference: Extract the authResult and get user info\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fpolicies\u002Frate-limits\"\u003EAuth0 API Rate Limit Policy\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"api-section\" data-section=\"none\"\u003E\n  \u003Ch1 id=\"saml\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"1\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003ESAML\u003C\u002Fh1\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe SAML protocol is used for 3rd party SaaS applications mostly, like Salesforce and Box. class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EAccount Linking\u003C\u002Fh1\u003E\n\u003Ch2 id=\"link\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"2\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003ELink\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Ch5 class=\"code-snippet-title\"\u003EExamples\u003C\u002Fh5\u003E\n\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-http\"\u003EGET https:\u002F\u002F__AUTH0_NAMESPACE__\u002Fauthorize?\n endpoint is \u003Cstrong\u003Edeprecated\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E for account linking. The \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi\u002Fmanagement\u002Fv2#!\u002FUsers\u002Fpost_identities\"\u003EPOST \u002Fapi\u002Fv2\u002Fusers\u002F{id}\u002Fidentities\u003C\u002Fa\u003E should be used instead. &quot;admin@example.com&quot;}\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor a regular web app, you should set the \u003Ccode\u003EadditionalParameters\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E: set the \u003Ccode\u003Eresponse_type\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E to be \u003Ccode\u003Ecode\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, the \u003Ccode\u003Ecallback_url\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E to be the callback url to which Auth0 will redirect with the authorization code, and the \u003Ccode\u003Escope\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E to be the JWT claims that you want included in the JWT.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"more-information\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"4\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EMore Information\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fuser-profile\u002Fuser-impersonation\"\u003EImpersonation\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan data-section-label=\"api-authz\"\u003EAPI Authorization\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"api-section\" data-section=\"api-authz\"\u003E\n  \u003Ch1 id=\"authorize-client\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"1\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EAuthorize Client\u003C\u002Fh1\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETo begin an OAuth 2.0 Authorization flow, your Client application should first send the user to the authorization URL.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe purpose of this call is to obtain consent from the user to invoke the API (specified in \u003Ccode\u003Eaudience\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E) and do certain things (specified in \u003Ccode\u003Escope\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E) on behalf of the user. Auth0 will authenticate the user and obtain consent, unless consent has been previously given. If you alter the value in \u003Ccode\u003Escope\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, Auth0 will require consent to be given again.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe OAuth 2.0 flows that require user authorization are:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Fgrant\u002Fauthorization-code\"\u003EAuthorization Code Grant\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Fgrant\u002Fauthorization-code-pkce\"\u003EAuthorization Code Grant using Proof Key for Code Exchange (PKCE)\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Fgrant\u002Fimplicit\"\u003EImplicit Grant\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOn the other hand, the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Fgrant\u002Fpassword\"\u003EResource Owner Password Grant\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Fgrant\u002Fclient-credentials\"\u003EClient Credentials\u003C\u002Fa\u003E flows do not use this endpoint since there is no user authorization involved. Instead they invoke directly the \u003Ccode\u003EPOST \u002Foauth\u002Ftoken\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E endpoint to retrieve an access token.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBased on the OAuth 2.0 flow you are implementing, the parameters slightly change. To determine which flow is best suited for your case refer to: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Fwhich-oauth-flow-to-use\"\u003EWhich OAuth 2.0 flow should I use?\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2 id=\"authorization-code-grant\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"2\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EAuthorization Code Grant\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Ch5 class=\"code-snippet-title\"\u003EExamples\u003C\u002Fh5\u003E\n\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-http\"\u003EGET https:\u002F\u002F__AUTH0_NAMESPACE__\u002Fauthorize?\n state=STATE\n\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fpre\u003E\n\u003Cblockquote\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ERESPONSE SAMPLE\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fblockquote\u003E\n\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-text\"\u003EHTTP\u002F1.1 302 Found\nLocation: __AUTH0_CALLBACK__?code=AUTHORIZATION_CODE&amp;state=STATE\n\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fpre\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ch5 class=\"http-method-box\"\u003E\n  \u003Cspan class=\"badge badge-primary\" href=\"#authorization-code-grant\"\u003EGET\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n  \u003Cspan class=\"path\" href=\"#authorization-code-grant\"\u003E\u002Fauthorize\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fh5\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis is the OAuth 2.0 grant that regular web apps utilize in order to access an API.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"request-parameters\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"3\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EDescription\u003C\u002Fth\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fthead\u003E\n\u003Ctbody\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eaudience\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EThe unique identifier of the target API you want to access.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Escope\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EThe scopes which you want to request authorization for. These must be separated by a space. You can request any of the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fopenid.net\u002Fspecs\u002Fopenid-connect-core-1_0.html#StandardClaims\"\u003Estandard OIDC scopes\u003C\u002Fa\u003E about users, such as \u003Ccode\u003Eprofile\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and \u003Ccode\u003Eemail\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, custom claims that must \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Ftutorials\u002Fadoption\u002Fscope-custom-claims\"\u003Econform to a namespaced format\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, or any scopes supported by the target API (for example, \u003Ccode\u003Eread:contacts\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E). Include \u003Ccode\u003Eoffline_access\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E to get a refresh token.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eresponse_type\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label label-danger\"\u003ERequired\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EIndicates to Auth0 which OAuth 2.0 flow you want to perform. Use \u003Ccode\u003Ecode\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E for Authorization Code Grant Flow.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eclient_id\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label label-danger\"\u003ERequired\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EYour application's Client ID.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Estate\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label label-primary\"\u003ERecommended\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EAn opaque value the clients adds to the initial request that Auth0 includes when redirecting the back to the client. This value must be used by the client to prevent CSRF attacks.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eredirect_uri\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EThe URL to which Auth0 will redirect the browser after authorization has been granted by the user.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eprompt\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003ETo initiate a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Ftutorials\u002Fsilent-authentication\"\u003Esilent authentication\u003C\u002Fa\u003E request, use \u003Ccode\u003Eprompt=none\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E (see Remarks for more info).\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftbody\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftable\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"test-with-authentication-api-debugger\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"4\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003ETest with Authentication API Debugger\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EYou can use our \u003Cstrong\u003EAuthentication API Debugger\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fextensions\u002Fauthentication-api-debugger\"\u003EAuthentication API Debugger extension\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EClick on \u003Cstrong\u003EInstall Debugger\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E to go to the article that explains how (you only have to do this once).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"test-endpoint-box\"\u003E\n  \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fextensions\u002Fauthentication-api-debugger\" class=\"btn btn-primary\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EInstall Debugger\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EIf you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe link varies according to your tenant's region: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002F__AUTH0_TENANT__.us.webtask.io\u002Fauth0-authentication-api-debugger\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EUS West\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002F__AUTH0_TENANT__.eu.webtask.io\u002Fauth0-authentication-api-debugger\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EEurope Central\u003C\u002Fa\u003E or \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002F__AUTH0_TENANT__.au.webtask.io\u002Fauth0-authentication-api-debugger\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EAustralia\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Col\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAt the \u003Cem\u003EConfiguration\u003C\u002Fem\u003E tab, set the \u003Cstrong\u003EClient\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E field to the client you want to use for the test.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ECopy the \u003Cstrong\u003ECallback URL\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E and set it as part of the \u003Cstrong\u003EAllowed Callback URLs\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E of your \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmanage.auth0.com\u002F#\u002Fclients\u002F__AUTH0_CLIENT_ID__\u002Fsettings\"\u003EClient Settings\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAt the \u003Cem\u003EOAuth2 \u002F OIDC\u003C\u002Fem\u003E tab, set the fields \u003Cstrong\u003EAudience\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E (to the unique identifier of the API you want to access), \u003Cstrong\u003EResponse Type\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E (set to \u003Ccode\u003Ecode\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E) and enable the \u003Cstrong\u003EAudience\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E switch.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EClick \u003Cstrong\u003EOAuth \u002F OIDC Login\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E. Following the redirect, the URL will contain the authorization code. Note, that the code will be set at the \u003Cstrong\u003EAuthorization Code\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E field so you can proceed with exchanging it for an access token.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fol\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"remarks\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"5\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003ERemarks\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIn order to improve compatibility for client applications, Auth0 will now return profile information in a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fopenid.net\u002Fspecs\u002Fopenid-connect-core-1_0.html#StandardClaims\"\u003Estructured claim format as defined by the OIDC specification\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. This means that in order to add custom claims to ID tokens or access tokens, they must conform to a namespaced format to avoid possible collisions with standard OIDC claims. For example, if you choose the namespace \u003Ccode\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Ffoo.com\u002F\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and you want to add a custom claim named \u003Ccode\u003Emyclaim\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, you would name the claim \u003Ccode\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Ffoo.com\u002Fmyclaim\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, instead of \u003Ccode\u003Emyclaim\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EInclude \u003Ccode\u003Eoffline_access\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E to the \u003Ccode\u003Escope\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E request parameter to get a refresh token from \u003Ca href=\"#authorization-code\"\u003EPOST \u002Foauth\u002Ftoken\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Make sure that the \u003Cstrong\u003EAllow Offline Access\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E field is enabled in the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmanage.auth0.com\u002F#\u002Fapis\"\u003EAPI Settings\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe \u003Ccode\u003Eredirect_uri\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E value must be specified as a valid callback URL under your \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmanage.auth0.com\u002F#\u002Fclients\u002F__AUTH0_CLIENT_ID__\u002Fsettings\"\u003EClient's Settings\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ESilent authentication lets you perform an authentication flow where Auth0 will only reply with redirects, and never with a login page. When an access token has expired, silent authentication can be used to retrieve a new one without user interaction, assuming the user's SSO session has not expired.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"more-information\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"6\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EMore Information\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca Authorization Code Grant Flow\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fprotocols\u002Foauth2\u002Foauth-state\"\u003EUsing the State Parameter\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Ftutorials\u002Fsilent-authentication\"\u003ESilent Authentication\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Ch2 id=\"authorization-code-grant-pkce-\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"7\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EAuthorization Code Grant (PKCE)\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Ch5 class=\"code-snippet-title\"\u003EExamples\u003C\u002Fh5\u003E\n\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-http\"\u003EGET https:\u002F\u002F__AUTH0_NAMESPACE__\u002Fauthorize?\n code_challenge_method=S256\n\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fpre\u003E\n\u003Cblockquote\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ERESPONSE SAMPLE\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fblockquote\u003E\n\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-text\"\u003EHTTP\u002F1.1 302 Found\nLocation: __AUTH0_CALLBACK__?code=AUTHORIZATION_CODE\n\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fpre\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ch5 class=\"http-method-box\"\u003E\n  \u003Cspan class=\"badge badge-primary\" href=\"#authorization-code-grant-pkce-\"\u003EGET\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n  \u003Cspan class=\"path\" href=\"#authorization-code-grant-pkce-\"\u003E\u002Fauthorize\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fh5\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis is the OAuth 2.0 grant that mobile apps utilize in order to access an API. Before starting with this flow, you need to generate and store a \u003Ccode\u003Ecode_verifier\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, and using that, generate a \u003Ccode\u003Ecode_challenge\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E that will be sent in the authorization request.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"request-parameters\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"8\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003ERequest Parameters\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Ctable class=\"table\"\u003E\u003Cthead\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EParameter\u003C\u002Fth\u003E\n\u003Cth style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EDescription\u003C\u002Fth\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fthead\u003E\n\u003Ctbody\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eaudience\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EThe unique identifier of the target API you want to access.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Escope\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EThe scopes which you want to request authorization for. These must be separated by a space. You can request any of the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fopenid.net\u002Fspecs\u002Fopenid-connect-core-1_0.html#StandardClaims\"\u003Estandard OIDC scopes\u003C\u002Fa\u003E about users, such as \u003Ccode\u003Eprofile\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and \u003Ccode\u003Eemail\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, custom claims that must conform to a namespaced format, or any scopes supported by the target API (for example, \u003Ccode\u003Eread:contacts\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E). Include \u003Ccode\u003Eoffline_access\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E to get a refresh token.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eresponse_type\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label label-danger\"\u003ERequired\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EIndicates to Auth0 which OAuth 2.0 Flow you want to perform. Use \u003Ccode\u003Ecode\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E for Authorization Code Grant (PKCE) Flow.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eclient_id\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label label-danger\"\u003ERequired\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EYour application's Client ID.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Estate\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label label-primary\"\u003ERecommended\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EAn opaque value the clients adds to the initial request that Auth0 includes when redirecting the back to the client. This value must be used by the client to prevent CSRF attacks.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eredirect_uri\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EThe URL to which Auth0 will redirect the browser after authorization has been granted by the user.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Ecode_challenge_method\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label label-danger\"\u003ERequired\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EMethod used to generate the challenge. The PKCE spec defines two methods, \u003Ccode\u003ES256\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and \u003Ccode\u003Eplain\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, however, Auth0 supports only \u003Ccode\u003ES256\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E since the latter is discouraged.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Ecode_challenge\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label label-danger\"\u003ERequired\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EGenerated challenge from the \u003Ccode\u003Ecode_verifier\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eprompt\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003ETo initiate a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Ftutorials\u002Fsilent-authentication\"\u003Esilent authentication\u003C\u002Fa\u003E request, use \u003Ccode\u003Eprompt=none\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E (see Remarks for more info).\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftbody\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftable\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"test-with-authentication-api-debugger\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"9\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003ETest with Authentication API Debugger\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EYou can use our \u003Cstrong\u003EAuthentication API Debugger\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E extension to test this endpoint. In order to do so you need to be logged in and have installed the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fextensions\u002Fauthentication-api-debugger\"\u003EAuthentication API this once).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"test-endpoint-box\"\u003E\n  \u003Ca Debugger\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EIf you have already installed the extension, skip to the Authentication API Debugger.\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe link varies according to your tenant's region: \u003Ca set the \u003Cstrong\u003EClient\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E field to the client you want to use for the test.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ECopy the \u003Cstrong\u003ECallback URL\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E and set it as part of the \u003Cstrong\u003EAllowed Callback URLs\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E of your \u003Ca Settings\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAt the \u003Cem\u003EOAuth2 \u002F OIDC\u003C\u002Fem\u003E tab, set the fields \u003Cstrong\u003EAudience\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E (to the unique identifier of the API you want to access), \u003Cstrong\u003EResponse Type\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E (set to \u003Ccode\u003Ecode\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E) and enable the \u003Cstrong\u003EAudience\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E and \u003Cstrong\u003EPKCE\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E switches.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EClick \u003Cstrong\u003EOAuth \u002F OIDC Login\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E. Following the redirect, the URL will contain the authorization code. Note, that the code will be set at the \u003Cstrong\u003EAuthorization Code\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E field, and the \u003Cstrong\u003ECode Verifier\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E will be automatically set as well, so you can proceed with exchanging the code for an access token.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fol\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"remarks\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"10\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003ERemarks\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIn order to improve compatibility for client applications, Auth0 will now return profile information in a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fopenid.net\u002Fspecs\u002Fopenid-connect-core-1_0.html#StandardClaims\"\u003Estructured claim format as defined by the OIDC specification\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. This means that in order to add custom claims to ID tokens or access tokens, they must conform to a namespaced format to avoid possible collisions with standard OIDC claims. For example, if you choose the namespace \u003Ccode\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Ffoo.com\u002F\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and you want to add a custom claim named \u003Ccode\u003Emyclaim\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, you would name the claim \u003Ccode\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Ffoo.com\u002Fmyclaim\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, instead of \u003Ccode\u003Emyclaim\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EInclude \u003Ccode\u003Eoffline_access\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E to the \u003Ccode\u003Escope\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E request parameter to get a refresh token from \u003Ca href=\"#authorization-code-pkce-\"\u003EPOST \u002Foauth\u002Ftoken\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Make sure that the \u003Cstrong\u003EAllow Offline Access\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E field is enabled in the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmanage.auth0.com\u002F#\u002Fapis\"\u003EAPI Settings\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe \u003Ccode\u003Eredirect_uri\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E value must be specified as a valid callback URL under your \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmanage.auth0.com\u002F#\u002Fclients\u002F__AUTH0_CLIENT_ID__\u002Fsettings\"\u003EClient's Settings\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ESilent authentication lets you perform an authentication flow where Auth0 will only reply with redirects, and never with a login page. When an access token has expired, silent authentication can be used to retrieve a new one without user interaction, assuming the user's SSO session has not expired.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"more-information\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"11\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EMore Information\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca This value must be used by the client to prevent CSRF attacks.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eredirect_uri\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EThe URL to which Auth0 will redirect the browser after authorization has been granted by the user.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Enonce\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label label-primary\"\u003ERecommended\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EA string value which will be included in the ID token response from Auth0, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Ftutorials\u002Fnonce\"\u003Eused to prevent token replay attacks\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. It is required for \u003Ccode\u003Eresponse_type=id_token token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Econnection\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EThe name of the connection configured to your client.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eprompt\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003ETo initiate a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Ftutorials\u002Fsilent-authentication\"\u003Esilent authentication\u003C\u002Fa\u003E request, use \u003Ccode\u003Eprompt=none\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E (see Remarks for more info).\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftbody\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftable\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"test-with-authentication-api-debugger\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"14\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003ETest with Authentication API Debugger\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EYou can use our \u003Cstrong\u003EAuthentication API Debugger\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E extension to test this endpoint. set the \u003Cstrong\u003EClient\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E field to the client you want to use for the test.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ECopy the \u003Cstrong\u003EAudience\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E (to the unique identifier of the API you want to access), \u003Cstrong\u003EResponse Type\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E (set to \u003Cstrong\u003EOAuth \u002F OIDC Login\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fol\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"remarks\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan specified as a valid callback URL under your \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmanage.auth0.com\u002F#\u002Fclients\u002F__AUTH0_CLIENT_ID__\u002Fsettings\"\u003EClient's Settings\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIf \u003Ccode\u003Eresponse_type=token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, after the user authenticates with the provider, this will redirect them to your application callback URL while passing the \u003Ccode\u003Eaccess_token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E in the address \u003Ccode\u003Elocation.hash\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. This is used for Single Page Apps and on Native Mobile SDKs.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EThe Implicit Grant does not support the issuance of refresh tokens. You can use \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Ftutorials\u002Fsilent-authentication\"\u003ESilent Authentication\u003C\u002Fa\u003E instead.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIn order to improve compatibility for client applications, Auth0 will now return profile information in a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fopenid.net\u002Fspecs\u002Fopenid-connect-core-1_0.html#StandardClaims\"\u003Estructured claim format as defined by the OIDC specification\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. This means that in order to add custom claims to ID tokens or access tokens, they must conform to a namespaced format to avoid possible collisions with standard OIDC claims. For example, if you choose the namespace \u003Ccode\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Ffoo.com\u002F\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and you want to add a custom claim named \u003Ccode\u003Emyclaim\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, you would name the claim \u003Ccode\u003Ehttps:\u002F\u002Ffoo.com\u002Fmyclaim\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, instead of \u003Ccode\u003Emyclaim\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ESilent authentication lets you perform an authentication flow where Auth0 will only reply with redirects, and never with a login page. When an access token has expired, silent authentication can be used to retrieve a new one without user interaction, assuming the user's SSO session has not expired.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"more-information\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"16\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EMore Information\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Fgrant\u002Fimplicit\"\u003ECalling APIs from Client-side Web Apps\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Ftutorials\u002Fimplicit-grant\"\u003EExecuting the Implicit Grant Flow\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fprotocols\u002Foauth2\u002Foauth-state\"\u003EUsing the State Parameter\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Ftutorials\u002Fnonce\"\u003EMitigate replay attacks when using the Implicit Grant\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Ftutorials\u002Fsilent-authentication\"\u003ESilent Authentication\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"api-section\" data-section=\"api-authz\"\u003E\n  \u003Ch1 id=\"get-token\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"1\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EGet Token\u003C\u002Fh1\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EUse this endpoint to:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EGet an \u003Ccode\u003Eaccess_token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E in order to call an API. You can, optionally, retrieve an \u003Ccode\u003Eid_token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and a \u003Ccode\u003Erefresh_token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E as well.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ERefresh your in order to access an API. In this case, a \u003Ccode\u003Escope\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E parameter will be included in the response JSON.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIf you don't request specific scopes, all scopes defined for the audience will be returned due to the implied trust to the client in this grant. You can customize the scopes returned in a rule. For more information, refer to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Fgrant\u002Fpassword\"\u003ECalling APIs from Highly Trusted Clients\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003ETo add realm support set the \u003Ccode\u003Egrant_type\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E to \u003Ccode\u003Ehttp:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Foauth\u002Fgrant-type\u002Fpassword-realm\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, and the \u003Ccode\u003Erealm\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E to the realm the user belongs. This maps to a connection in Auth0. For example, if you have configured a database connection for your internal employees and you have named the connection \u003Ccode\u003Eemployees\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, then use this value. For more information on how to implement this refer to: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Ftutorials\u002Fpassword-grant#realm-support\"\u003ERealm Support\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIn addition to username and password, Auth0 may also require the end-user to provide an additional factor as proof of identity before issuing the requested scopes. In this case, the request described above will return an \u003Ccode\u003Emfa_required\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E error along with an \u003Ccode\u003Emfa_token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. You can use these tokens to request a challenge for the possession factor and validate it accordingly. For details refer to \u003Ca href=\"#resource-owner-password-and-mfa\"\u003EResource Owner Password and MFA\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"more-information\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"20\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EMore Information\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Fgrant\u002Fpassword\"\u003ECalling APIs from Highly Trusted Clients\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fapi-auth\u002Ftutorials\u002Fpassword-grant\"\u003EExecuting the Resource Owner Password Grant\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Ch2 id=\"resource-owner-password-and-mfa\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"21\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EResource Owner Password and MFA\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn addition to username and password, you may also ask your users to provide an additional factor as proof of identity before issuing the requested tokens.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe first step, is to request a challenge based on the challenge types supported by the Client application and the end-user (see next paragraph). This is an optional step, since it is not required if you already know that \u003Ccode\u003Eotp\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E is supported.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENext, you have to verify the MFA, using the \u003Ccode\u003E\u002Foauth\u002Ftoken\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E endpoint and the challenge type specified in the first step: an OTP code, a recovery code, or an OOB challenge.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"mfa-challenge-request\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"22\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon function (error, response, body) {\n  if (error) throw new Error(error);\n\n  console.log(body);\n});\n\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fpre\u003E\n\u003Cblockquote\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ERESPONSE SAMPLE FOR PENDING CHALLENGE:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fblockquote\u003E\n\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-JSON\"\u003EHTTP\u002F1.1 200 OK\nContent-Type: application\u002Fjson\n{\n class=\"http-method-box\"\u003E\n  \u003Cspan class=\"badge badge-success\" href=\"#resource-owner-password-and-mfa\"\u003EPOST\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n  \u003Cspan class=\"path\" href=\"#resource-owner-password-and-mfa\"\u003E\u002Foauth\u002Ftoken\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fh5\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETo verify MFA using an OOB challenge (e.g. Push \u002F SMS) your app must make a request to \u003Ccode\u003E\u002Foauth\u002Ftoken\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\nwith \u003Ccode\u003Egrant_type=http:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Foauth\u002Fgrant-type\u002Fmfa-oob\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. Include the \u003Ccode\u003Eoob_code\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E you received from the challenge response, as well as the \u003Ccode\u003Emfa_token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E you received as part of \u003Ccode\u003Emfa_required\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E error.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe response to this request depends on the status of the underlying challenge verification:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIf the challenge has been accepted and verified: it will be the same as for \u003Ccode\u003Epassword\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E or \u003Ccode\u003Ehttp:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Foauth\u002Fgrant-type\u002Fpassword-realm\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E grant types.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIf the challenge has been rejected, you will get an \u003Ccode\u003Einvalid_grant\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E error, meaning that the challenge was rejected by the user. At this point you should stop polling, as this response is final.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003EIf the challenge verification is still pending (meaning it has not been accepted nor rejected) you will get an \u003Ccode\u003Eauthorization_pending\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E error, meaning that you must retry the same request a few seconds later. If you request too frequently you will get a \u003Ccode\u003Eslow_down\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E error.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen the challenge response includes a \u003Ccode\u003Ebinding_method: prompt\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E your app needs to prompt the user for the \u003Ccode\u003Ebinding_code\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and send it as part of the request. The \u003Ccode\u003Ebinding_code\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E is a usually a 6 digit number (similar to an OTP) included as part of the challenge.  No \u003Ccode\u003Ebinding_code\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E is necessary if the challenge response did not include a \u003Ccode\u003Ebinding_method\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. In this scenario the response will be immediate; you will receive an \u003Ccode\u003Einvalid_grant\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E or an \u003Ccode\u003Eaccess_token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E as response.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch4 id=\"request-parameters\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"29\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003ERequest Parameters\u003C\u002Fh4\u003E\n\u003Ctable class=\"table\"\u003E\u003Cthead\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Cth style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EParameter\u003C\u002Fth\u003E\n\u003Cth style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EDescription\u003C\u002Fth\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fthead\u003E\n\u003Ctbody\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Egrant_type\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label label-danger\"\u003ERequired\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003EDenotes the flow you are using. \u003Ccode\u003EPost\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E or \u003Ccode\u003EBasic\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Emfa_token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label error.\u003C\u002Ftd\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ftr\u003E\n\u003Ctr\u003E\n\u003Ctd style=\"text-align:left\"\u003E\u003Ccode\u003Eoob_code\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E \u003Cbr\u002F\u003E\u003Cspan class=\"label &quot;abcdefg&quot;\n}\n\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fpre\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ch5 class=\"http-method-box\"\u003E\n  \u003Cspan class=\"badge badge-success\" recovery code to login. This method is supposed to be used to authenticate when the device you enrolled is not available, or you cannot received the challenge or accept it, for instance, due to connectivity issues.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETo verify MFA using a recovery code your app must prompt the user for the recovery code, and then make a request to \u003Ccode\u003Eoauth\u002Ftoken\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E with \u003Ccode\u003Egrant_type=http:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Foauth\u002Fgrant-type\u002Fmfa-recovery-code\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. Please see \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fclients\u002Fclient-grant-types\"\u003EClient Grant Types\u003C\u002Fa\u003E for more information.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EGiven the social provider's \u003Ccode\u003Eaccess_token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and the \u003Ccode\u003Econnection\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, this endpoint will authenticate the user with the provider and return a JSON with the \u003Ccode\u003Eaccess_token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and, optionally, an \u003Ccode\u003Eid_token\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. This endpoint only works for Facebook, Google, Twitter and Weibo.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"request-parameters\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"3\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + Each new request reduces this number by 1. For each minute that passes, requests are added back, so this number increases by 1 each time.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ccode\u003EX-RateLimit-Reset\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E: Remaining time until the rate limit (\u003Ccode\u003EX-RateLimit-Limit\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E) resets. The value is in \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fen.wikipedia.org\u002Fwiki\u002FUnix_time\"\u003EUTC epoch seconds\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"more-information\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"6\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EMore Information\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fuser-profile\u002Fuser-profile-details#api\"\u003EUser Profile: In-Depth Details - API\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Fpolicies\u002Frate-limits\"\u003EAuth0 API Rate Limit Policy\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n\u003Cdiv class=\"api-section\" data-section=\"legacy\"\u003E\n  \u003C!-- markdownlint-disable --\u003E\n\u003Ch1 id=\"delegation\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"1\" class=\"anchor\" href=\"#' + anchor + '\"\u003E\u003Ci class=\"icon icon-budicon-345\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EDelegation\u003C\u002Fh1\u003E\n\u003Ch5 class=\"code-snippet-title\"\u003EExamples\u003C\u002Fh5\u003E\n\u003Cpre\u003E\u003Ccode class=\"language-http\"\u003EPOST https:\u002F\u002F__AUTH0_NAMESPACE__\u002Fdelegation\nContent-Type: 'application\u002Fjson'\n{\n  &quot;client_id&quot;: &quot;__AUTH0_CLIENT_ID__&quot;,\n  &quot;grant_type&quot;: &quot;urn:ietf:params:oauth:grant-type:jwt-bearer&quot;,\n  &quot;id_token&quot; For a sample in version 7 of the library, refer to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fauth0.com\u002Fdocs\u002Flibraries\u002Fauth0js\u002Fv7#delegation-token-request\"\u003EDelegation Token Request\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis endpoint limits up to 10 requests per minute from the same IP address with the same \u003Ccode\u003Euser_id\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis endpoint will return three HTTP Response Headers, that provide relevant data on its rate limits:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cul\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ccode\u003EX-RateLimit-Limit\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E: Number of requests allowed per minute.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ccode\u003EX-RateLimit-Remaining\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E: Number of requests available. Each new request reduces this number by 1. For each minute that passes, requests are added back, so this number increases by 1 each time.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ccode\u003EX-RateLimit-Reset\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E: Remaining time until the rate limit (\u003Ccode\u003EX-RateLimit-Limit\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E) resets. The value is in \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fen.wikipedia.org\u002Fwiki\u002FUnix_time\"\u003EUTC epoch seconds\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003Ch3 id=\"more-information\" class=\"anchor-heading\"\u003E\u003Cspan id=\"6\"
